Time of Udhiyah Slaughter: City vs. Village
Ruling on when city dwellers vs. villagers may slaughter udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the time of udhiyah slaughter for city dwellers versus villagers, identify the proof from hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
The time for udhiyah begins at dawn; the Eid prayer is a condition only for city dwellers.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a key distinction in the Hanafi school regarding the timing of udhiyah sacrifice. While a famous hadith seems to require slaughtering after the Eid prayer, the Hanafi jurists interpret this as specific to those who attend the prayer. Villagers who do not perform the Eid congregational prayer follow the original time starting from Fajr. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on when city dwellers and villagers may slaughter the udhiyah. Note the key distinction: city dwellers must wait until after the Eid prayer; villagers may slaughter after dawn.
The matn says: 'And a city dweller should not slaughter before the prayer, and the slaughter of others [is permissible].'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that al-Shafi'i and Malik hold that villagers also must wait until after the Imam's prayer. They generalize the hadith to all Muslims.
The text says: 'This is an argument against al-Shafi'i and Malik in their denial of the permissibility after the servant's prayer before the Imam's slaughter.'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opposing school uses the apparent generality of the hadith: 'Whoever slaughters before the Imam's prayer, let him repeat his sacrifice.' They apply it to everyone.
The hadith does not explicitly exclude villagers.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith is specified by another saying: 'The first of our rituals today is the prayer, then the sacrifice.' This implies the prayer is for those who are obliged to pray. Villagers are not obliged to perform the Eid prayer in congregation, so the original time (dawn) applies to them.
Also, the time for udhiyah begins at dawn; the delay for city dwellers is due to a condition (the prayer), not the time itself.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under Hanafi, villagers may sacrifice early and eat from the meat before the Eid prayer. Under Shafi'i/Maliki, they must wait until after the Imam's prayer.
This affects families in rural areas who may want to distribute meat early.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولا يذبح مصري قبل الصلاة وذبح غيره) يعني لا يجوز لأهل المصر أن يذبحوا الأضحية قبل أن يصلوا صلاة العيد ويجوز لأهل القرى والبادية أن يذبحوا بعد صلاة الفجر قبل أن يصلي الإمام صلاة العيد والأصل في ذلك قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من ذبح قبل صلاة الإمام فليعد ذبيحته، ومن ذبح بعد صلاة الإمام فقد تم نسكه وأصاب سنة المسلمين» قال صاحب النهاية : هذا يشير إلى ما ذكر في المبسوط حيث قال : لا يجزيه لعدم الشرط لا لعدم الوقت. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام «أول نسكنا هذا اليوم الصلاة ثم الأضحية» وهذا في ظاهر في حق من عليه الصلاة فبقي غيره على الأصل فيذبح بعد طلوع الفجر وهو حجة على الشافعي ومالك في نفيهما الجواز بعد صلاة العبد قبل نحر الإمام والمعتبر في ذلك مكان الأضحية حتى لو كانت في السواد والمضحي في المصر يجوز كما انشق الفجر، وفي العكس لا يجوز إلا بعد الصلاة وحيلة المصري إذا أراد التعجيل أن يبعث بها إلى خارج المصر في موضع يجوز للمسافر أن يقصر فيضحي فيه كما طلع الفجر لأن وقتها من طلوع الفجر وإنما أخرت في حق المصر لما ذكرنا، ولأنها تشبه الزكاة فيعتبر في الأداء مكان المحل وهو لإمكان الفاعل بخلاف صدقة الفطر حيث يعتبر فيها مكان الفاعل لأنها تتعلق بالذمة والمال البحر الرائق ج / م٢١ المال
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (And a city dweller should not slaughter before the prayer, and the slaughter of others [is permissible]). Meaning, it is not permissible for the people of the city to slaughter the udhiyah before they perform the Eid prayer, and it is permissible for the people of villages and desert to slaughter after the Fajr prayer before the Imam performs the Eid prayer. The basis for that is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever slaughters before the Imam's prayer, let him repeat his sacrifice; and whoever slaughters after the Imam's prayer has completed his ritual and followed the Sunnah of the Muslims.' The author of al-Nihayah said: This refers to what was mentioned in al-Mabsut where he said: It does not suffice due to lack of a condition, not due to lack of time. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'The first of our rituals on this day is the prayer, then the sacrifice.' This is apparent with respect to the one upon whom the prayer is obligatory; so others remain on the original ruling, so they slaughter after dawn. This is an argument against al-Shafi'i and Malik in their denial of the permissibility after the servant's prayer before the Imam's slaughter. The consideration is the location of the sacrifice; so even if it is in the countryside and the sacrificer is in the city, it is permissible when dawn breaks. Conversely, it is not permissible except after the prayer. And a trick (hilah) for the city dweller if he wants to expedite is to send it outside the city to a place where a traveler may shorten prayers, and sacrifice there as soon as dawn breaks, because its time begins at dawn. It was only delayed for the city dweller due to what we mentioned, and because it resembles zakat, so the location of the wealth is considered in performance, which is possible for the actor, unlike sadaqat al-fitr where the location of the actor is considered because it is a liability and wealth. Al-Bahr al-Raiq, vol. 8, p. 321.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the matn that states the ruling on the time of slaughter for udhiyah. The matn says: 'A city dweller should not slaughter before the prayer, and the slaughter of others [is allowed].' The commentator explains that city dwellers (ahl al-misr) may not slaughter until after the Eid prayer, while villagers (ahl al-qura) may slaughter after dawn on Eid day, even before the Imam's prayer. The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever slaughters before the Imam's prayer, let him repeat his sacrifice; and whoever slaughters after the Imam's prayer has completed his ritual.' The commentator clarifies that this ruling is about condition (shart) not time (waqt)—meaning the time is valid from dawn, but the city dweller must wait for the prayer as a condition for validity. The hadith 'The first of our rituals today is the prayer, then the sacrifice' implies that the prayer is prior for those who are obliged to pray. This is used as an argument against al-Shafi'i and Malik, who deny the permissibility of slaughter for villagers before the Imam's slaughter. The decisive factor is the location of the animal: if the animal is in a village and the owner is in the city, it is permissible to slaughter at dawn. Conversely, if the animal is in the city, it must wait. A legal trick (hīla) for a city dweller who wants to hasten is to send the animal to a place outside the city where a traveler may shorten prayers, and sacrifice there at dawn, because the time starts at dawn. The delay for the city dweller is due to the required prayer. The commentator likens this to zakat, where the location of the wealth (the animal) determines the ruling, unlike sadaqat al-fitr which follows the location of the person.

Key Terms
مصري (miṣrī): A person residing in a city (misr) where Friday and Eid prayers are established
قرية (qarya): A village or rural area where the Eid prayer is not necessarily performed in congregation
حيلة (ḥīla): A permissible stratagem to achieve a legal aim, here to allow early slaughter for a city dweller

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can a villager slaughter his udhiyah on Eid al-Adha?
A) Only after the Eid prayer.
B) After dawn on Eid day, even before the Eid prayer.
C) After the Imam slaughters.
D) Only at midday.

Key Takeaway
The time for udhiyah slaughter begins at dawn, but city dwellers must wait until after the Eid prayer; villagers may slaughter immediately after dawn.

Consideration of Place and Legal Trick for Early Sacrifice
Explains that the location of the animal matters and a city dweller can send the animal to a village to sacrifice early.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that the time of udhiyah depends on the location of the animal and apply the legal trick (hila) for a city dweller to sacrifice early.

Core Idea
The time of sacrifice is determined by the animal's location, not the person's.

In this passage, the commentator explains that the consideration for the time of udhiyah (sacrifice) is the place of the animal, not the place of the sacrificer. This leads to a practical legal device (hila) for a city dweller who wishes to sacrifice before the Eid prayer: he sends the animal to a village where sacrifice is permitted at dawn. The ruling is derived by analogy (qiyas) with zakat, where the place of the property matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the first sentence: 'المعتبر في ذلك مكان الأضحية'. This establishes that the time of sacrifice is based on the animal's location.
This is the key principle.
2
Analyze the two scenarios
If the animal is in the countryside and the sacrificer is in the city, sacrifice is allowed at dawn. If the animal is in the city, it is not allowed until after the Eid prayer.
Contrast the two cases.
3
Understand the legal trick
A city dweller can send his animal outside the city limits (to a place where a traveler may shorten prayers) and sacrifice it there at dawn.
This is the hila mentioned.
4
Examine the proof via qiyas
The passage draws an analogy with zakat: both are financial acts of worship where the location of the property matters. The illa (effective cause) is that the property can be physically located elsewhere and it is possible for the owner to perform the act there.
Contrast with sadaqat al-fitr, which is a personal obligation.
5
Note the distinction from sadaqat al-fitr
Sadaqat al-fitr is based on the person's location because it is a liability on the person (tata'allaqu bi al-dhimmah), unlike udhiyah which involves a physical property.
This sharpens the understanding of the illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمعتبر في ذلك مكان الأضحية حتى لو كانت في السواد والمضحي في المصر يجوز كما انشق الفجر، وفي العكس لا يجوز إلا بعد الصلاة وحيلة المصري إذا أراد التعجيل أن يبعث بها إلى خارج المصر في موضع يجوز للمسافر أن يقصر فيضحي فيه كما طلع الفجر لأن وقتها من طلوع الفجر وإنما أخرت في حق المصر لما ذكرنا، ولأنها تشبه الزكاة فيعتبر في الأداء مكان المحل وهو لإمكان الفاعل بخلاف صدقة الفطر حيث يعتبر فيها مكان الفاعل لأنها تتعلق بالذمة والمال ليس بمحل لها.
The consideration in this matter is the location of the udhiyah, so if the animal is in the countryside and the sacrificer is in the city, it is permissible as soon as dawn breaks, and in the opposite case it is not permissible except after the prayer. And the legal trick for the city dweller if he wishes to hasten is to send it outside the city to a place where a traveler may shorten the prayer, and sacrifice there as soon as dawn rises, because its time is from dawn, and it was delayed only for the city dweller for the reason we mentioned. And because it resembles zakat, so performance is considered according to the location of the property, as it is possible for the doer, unlike sadaqat al-fitr where the location of the doer is considered because it is incumbent on the person, and the property is not a place for it.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the matn. It addresses the consideration of location in determining the permissibility of early sacrifice. The key principle is that 'the consideration is given to the place of the udhiyah (the animal), not the place of the person.' Therefore, if a city dweller keeps his animal in the countryside, it may be sacrificed as soon as dawn breaks, because the animal's location is in the village. Conversely, if a villager brings his animal to the city, he must wait for the Eid prayer. The passage then presents a legal device (hila) for a city dweller who wishes to sacrifice early: he sends the animal outside the city limits (to a place where a traveler may shorten prayers), and sacrifices it there at dawn. This is permissible because the time for sacrifice begins at dawn; the restriction for city dwellers is only due to the prayer obligation in the city. The commentator draws an analogy with zakat, where the place of the property matters for payment, contrasting with sadaqat al-fitr where it is a personal obligation on the person.

Key Terms
حيلة (hila): A legal device to achieve a permissible result while complying with the letter of the law; here, sending the animal to the countryside to enable early sacrifice.
مكان الأضحية (makan al-udhiyah): The location where the sacrificial animal is situated at the time of slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A city dweller wants to sacrifice his udhiyah before the Eid prayer. He keeps his sheep in a village outside the city. According to the passage, can he sacrifice it at dawn?
A) Yes, because the animal is in the village where sacrifice is allowed at dawn.
B) No, because he is a city dweller and must wait for the prayer.
C) Only if he goes to the village himself.
D) He must bring the animal to the city and wait.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of early sacrifice on Eid day depends on the location of the animal, not the sacrificer, and a city dweller can circumvent the post-prayer restriction by sending the animal to the countryside.

Days of Udhiyah and Its Superiority over Charity
Specifies the days of sacrifice and emphasizes the superiority of the act over its monetary value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the days of udhiyah, identify the best day, explain why the sacrifice itself is better than giving its value in charity, and apply the compensation rules for a missed sacrifice.

Core Idea
Sacrificing the animal is superior to giving its price in charity because it is a time-bound worship that cannot be replaced.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the timing of the udhiyah sacrifice and its legal superiority over simply giving money in charity. It also outlines the consequences for those who fail to sacrifice within the prescribed days, distinguishing between wealthy and poor individuals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time window
The sacrifice is valid only on three specific days: the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah. The first day (Eid) is the most virtuous.
Slaughtering at night is permissible but disliked due to possible error in darkness.
2
Distinguish between days of Nahr and Tashriq
Understand that the four days (10-13) are divided: day 10 only for sacrifice, day 13 only for tashriq (drying meat), and the middle two for both.
The 13th is not a day for sacrifice according to the Hanafi school.
3
Understand the preference of sacrifice over charity
The text emphasizes that performing the actual sacrifice is better than giving its value in charity. For the wealthy, udhiyah is wajib; for the poor, it is sunnah. Charity is purely voluntary.
The act of sacrifice is time-bound and cannot be made up, unlike charity which can be given at any time.
4
Apply the compensation rule for missed sacrifice
If a wealthy person does not sacrifice during the three days, he must give the market value of the animal in charity. If a poor person had already purchased an animal, he must give that animal in charity.
If no animal was purchased, the poor person has no obligation.
5
Consider special cases of date confusion
If the imam mistakenly prays Eid on Arafa and people sacrifice based on reliable testimony, it is valid. If they were in doubt they must repeat both prayer and sacrifice. Slaughtering after noon on Arafa that turns out to be Eid is valid.
The last part of the text about nights and dawn is garbled in the source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووقتها ثلاثة أيام أولها أفضلها ويجوز الذبح في لياليها إلا أنه يكره لاحتمال الغلط في الظلمة. وأيام النحر ثلاثة. وأيام التشريق ثلاثة والكل تمضي بمضي أربعة أيام أولها نحر لا غير، وآخرها تشريق لا غير، والمتوسطان نحر وتشريق. والتضحية فيها أفضل من التصدق بثمنها لأنها تقع واجبة إن كان غنياً، وسنة إن كان فقيراً. والتصدق بالثمن تطوع محض فكانت هي أفضل لأنها تفوت بفوات أيامها، ولو لم يضح حتى مضت أيامها وكان غنياً وجب عليه أن يتصدق بالقيمة، سواء اشتراها أو لم يشترها. وإن كان فقيراً فإن كان اشتراها وجب عليه التصدق بها، ولو ذبح بعد الزوال يوم عرفة ثم ظهر أنه يوم النحر يجزيه، وفي سائر الأوقات جعل الليل رفة فهي متأخرة عنها وليلة النحر الأول هي ليلة النحر الثاني، وليلة النحر الثاني هي ليلة النحر الثالث، وليلة النحر الثالث ليلة الفجر الثالث عشر حتى يجوز الذبح فيها قبل طلوع الفجر؛ كذا في المحيط . وفي النوازل: الإمام إذا صلى العيد يوم عرفة وضحى الناس فهذا على وجهين : إما أن شهد عند الشهود أولاً بأنه يوم النحر ففي الأول تجوز الصلاة والأضحية وفي الثاني لا تجوز ولو شكوا في يوم النحر فصلى بهم الإمام وضحوا ثم علموا في الغد أنه يوم عرفة فإنه عليه إعادة الصلاة والأضحية جميعاً. وفي عرفة وهو يرى أنه يوم يوم سابق على النهار إلا في يوم عر هي
And its time is three days, the first of them is the best, and slaughtering in their nights is permissible except that it is disliked due to the possibility of error in darkness. And the days of sacrifice are three. And the days of tashriq are three, and all pass by the passage of four days: the first is only for sacrifice, the last is only for tashriq, and the middle two are for sacrifice and tashriq. And sacrificing in them is better than giving charity of their price, because it occurs as obligatory if one is wealthy, and as sunnah if one is poor. And giving charity of the price is pure supererogation, so it is better because it is missed by missing its days. And if one did not sacrifice until its days passed and he is wealthy, he is obliged to give charity of the value, whether he had purchased it or not. And if he is poor, if he had purchased it, he is obliged to give it in charity. And if one slaughtered after noon on the day of Arafa and then it appeared that it was the day of Nahr, it is valid. And in all other times, the night is made before the day except on the day of Arafa: the night is later than it. And the first night of sacrifice is the night of the second day of sacrifice, and the night of the second day of sacrifice is the night of the third day of sacrifice, and the night of the third day of sacrifice is the night of the dawn of the thirteenth until it is permissible to slaughter therein before dawn; thus in al-Muhit. And in al-Nawazil: If the imam prayed the Eid prayer on the day of Arafa and the people sacrificed, this is of two types: Either they witnessed before the witnesses firstly that it was the day of Nahr, so in the first the prayer and sacrifice are valid, and in the second they are not valid. And if they doubted about the day of Nahr, then the imam prayed with them and they sacrificed, then they knew the next day that it was the day of Arafa, then he must repeat both the prayer and the sacrifice. And on Arafa and he thinks it is the day... previous to the day except on the day of... she.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This final section of the window covers several important points about the time and virtue of udhiyah. First, the time for sacrifice extends over three days: the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah. The first day (Eid day) is the most virtuous. Slaughtering at night is permissible but disliked due to the risk of mistake. The days of tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th) are different: the first day of Nahr is only for sacrifice, the last day (13th) is only for tashriq (drying meat), and the middle two are for both. Second, the passage emphasizes that performing the actual sacrifice is superior to giving its value in charity. This is because for a wealthy person the udhiyah is wajib, while charity is nafl; and even for a poor person it is sunnah. Moreover, the act of sacrifice is time-bound and cannot be made up after its days, unlike charity which can be given anytime. If one fails to sacrifice and is wealthy, he must give the value in charity; if poor and had bought an animal, he must give that animal in charity. Third, there are special rulings for the case of Arafa and Eid when there is confusion about the date: slaughtering after noon on Arafa, if it turns out to be Eid, the sacrifice is valid. The nights of the days of sacrifice are considered: the night of the 10th is the night of the 11th, etc., allowing sacrifice up to dawn of the 13th. Finally, the text discusses the scenario where the imam mistakenly prays Eid on Arafa and people sacrifice: if they had reliable testimony that it was Eid, it is valid; otherwise not. If they were in doubt, both prayer and sacrifice must be repeated. The last part is corrupted and unclear.

Key Terms
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The three days of sacrifice: the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhu al-Hijjah; called so because meat is dried in the sun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling for a wealthy person who fails to sacrifice during the three days of Nahr?
A) He must give the value of the animal in charity.
B) He does nothing; the obligation falls away.
C) He must sacrifice on the 13th.
D) He must give away the animal itself whether he bought one or not.

Key Takeaway
The udhiyah sacrifice must be performed within its three days; if missed by a wealthy person, the value must be given in charity.

Permissible and Impermissible Defects in Sacrificial Animals
Lists acceptable and unacceptable defects with hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between acceptable and unacceptable defects in an udhiyah animal according to Hanafi fiqh, and apply the hadith proof to classify new cases.

Core Idea
An udhiyah animal is invalid only if a defect clearly undermines its health or flesh; minor or natural defects are acceptable.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rulings on defects in sacrificial animals (udhiyah). The text from Al-Hidayah lists both permissible and impermissible conditions, supported by a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for ensuring the validity of your sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Udhiyah is wajib for the wealthy and sunnah for others. The defects discussed affect the validity of the sacrifice.
Focus on the animal's condition, not the obligation level.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib lists four animals that are not permissible: the obviously one-eyed, obviously sick, obviously emaciated, and lame that cannot walk.
Hadith is reported by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The negation 'لا تجوز' indicates impermissibility; 'al-bayyin' requires the defect to be obvious.
Minor or hidden defects are not included.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers udhiyah sunnah, not wajib, but agrees on the four major defects.
Practical difference: obligation level, not defect rules.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text provides detailed conditions (e.g., degree of lameness) based on Hanafi usul, with the mufta bihi as stated.
Relied-upon position in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( ويضحي بالجماء) التي لا قرن لها يعني خلقة لأن القرن لا يتعلق به مقصود، وكذا مكسورة القرن بل أولى قال رحمه الله : (والخصي) وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ضحى بكبشين أملحين أولى لأن لحمه أطيب وقد صح موجوأين. الأملح الذي فيه ملحة وهو البياض الذي فيه شعيرات سود وهو من لون الملح، والموجوء المخصي من الوجء وهو أن يضرب عروق الخصية بشيء. وفي المحيط : وتجوز الجرباء وفي تجوز الحاوي : الجرباء إذا كانت سمينة ا هـ . قال رحمه الله : (والتولاء) وهي المجنونة لأنه يخل بالمقصود إذا كانت تعتلف، فإن كانت سمينة ولم يتلف جلدها جاز لأنه لا يخل بالمقصود قال : ولا يجوز بالهتماء التي لا أسنان لها إن كانت لا تعتلف، وإن كانت تعتلف جاز وهو الصحيح ولا الجلالة التي تأكل العذراء ولا تأكل غيرها، ولا مقطوعة الضرع ولا التي لا تستطيع أن ترضع ولدها ولا التي يبس ضرعها، ولا مقطوعة الأنف والذنب والطرف؛ كذا في المحيط . قال رحمه الله : (لا بالعمياء والعوراء والعجفاء والعرجاء) أي التي لا تمشي إلى المنسك أي إلى المذبح لما روي عن البراء بن عازب أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قال أربع لا تجوز في الأضاحي العوراء البين عورها والمريضة البين مرضها، والعجفاء البين ضلعها والكسيرة التي لا تنقى(۱) رواه أبو داود والنسائي وجماعة أخر وصححه الترمذي. وفي الحاوي قال :مشايخنا العرجاء التي تمشي بثلاثة قوائم وتجافي الرابع عن الأرض لا تجوز الأضحية بها، وإن كانت تضع الرابع على الأرض وتستعين به إلا أنها ذلك وتضعه وضعاً خفيفاً يجوز، وإن كانت ترفعه رفعاً أو تحمل المنكسر لا تجوز . تتمايل مع وفي الخانية : وكذا الحولاء التي في عينها حول، ولا تجوز المنفسخة العين وهي التي غارت عينها اهـ. قال رحمه الله : (ومقطوعة أكثر الإذان أو الذئب أو العين أو الألية) لقول علي
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And he sacrifices with the hornless) meaning one that has no horn by creation because the horn is not connected to the intended purpose, and likewise the broken-horned, rather more so. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the castrated). From Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that he, peace and blessings be upon him, sacrificed two white-and-black hornless rams, it is better because its meat is more delicious, and it is authentically reported 'mawju'an'. Al-Amlah is that which has white with black hairs, like the color of salt; al-mawju' is the castrated from al-waj' which is to strike the veins of the testicle with something. In al-Muhit: The mangy is permissible, and in al-Hawi: The mangy if it is fat. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And al-Tawla') which is the insane, because it disrupts the intended purpose if it cannot graze; if it is fat and its skin is not damaged, it is permissible because it does not disrupt the purpose. He said: And it is not permissible with al-Hatma' which has no teeth if it cannot graze; if it can graze it is permissible, and that is the correct view. Nor the Jalalah that eats filth and does not eat other, nor the one with cut udder, nor the one that cannot suckle its young, nor the one whose udder is dry, nor the one with cut nose, tail, or limb; thus in al-Muhit. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (Not with the blind, the one-eyed, the emaciated, and the lame) meaning those that cannot walk to the place of sacrifice, because of what is narrated from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib that he, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Four are not permissible in sacrifices: the obviously one-eyed, the obviously sick, the obviously emaciated, and the lame that cannot walk.' Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i and others, and al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. In al-Hawi: Our shuyukh said: The lame that walks on three legs and keeps the fourth off the ground is not permissible for sacrifice; if it places the fourth on the ground and uses it but places it lightly, it is permissible; if it lifts it up or carries the broken one, it is not permissible. And in al-Khaniyyah: Likewise the one with a squint (hawla'), and the one with depressed eye is not permissible. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the one with most of the ear or the tail or the eye or the fat tail cut off) because of the saying of 'Ali.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage explains the defects that are acceptable and those that prevent the validity of the udhiyah. The author begins with the hornless animal (al-jamma'), stating that it is permissible because the horn does not serve any essential purpose. Similarly, the broken-horned animal is even more permissible. Then the castrated animal (al-khasi) is discussed, with a preference for the castrated ram due to better meat, citing that the Prophet ﷺ sacrificed castrated rams. Next, the mangy animal (al-jarba') is permissible if fat. The insane animal (al-tawla') is permissible if it is fat and its skin is not damaged, otherwise not. Al-Hatma' (toothless) is impermissible if it cannot graze, but permissible if it can. Al-Jalalah (eating filth) is impermissible if it only eats filth. Animals with cut udders, inability to suckle, dry udders, or cut nose, tail, or limb are impermissible. Then the four major defects from the hadith of al-Bara': blindness, one-eye, emaciation, and lameness are explained. Lameness is specified: if the animal cannot walk properly on three legs, it is not valid; if it places the fourth leg lightly, it is valid. Additionally, squint and depressed eye are impermissible. Finally, cutting off most of the ear, tail, eye, or fat tail is also impermissible, based on a saying of 'Ali.

Key Terms
الجماء (al-jamma'): An animal born without horns, as opposed to one with horns broken.
التولاء (al-tawla'): An insane animal that cannot graze properly.
العجفاء (al-'ajfa'): A severely emaciated animal with little flesh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith mentioned, which of the following is NOT among the four animals that are not permissible for sacrifice?
A) The obviously one-eyed
B) The obviously sick
C) The lame that cannot walk
D) The broken-horned

Key Takeaway
A sacrifice is valid only if the animal is free from the four major defects specified in the hadith, and from other clear impairments that undermine its health or ability to graze.

The Four Major Defects Invalidating Sacrifice
Citing the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib on four defects that render an animal invalid for sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four major defects that invalidate a sacrifice animal according to the Hanafi school and apply the graded ruling on lameness.

Core Idea
Four defects invalidate sacrifice: obvious blindness, illness, emaciation, and a broken leg that cannot walk.

All animals are permissible for udhiyah except those with specific defects that render them incomplete. The Hanafi school derives these defects from a prophetic hadith and further qualifies them based on severity. This lesson guides you through the four defects, the proof, and the critical nuance on lameness that determines validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that the act is udhiyah (sacrificial slaughter). The ruling is that the four listed defects render the animal invalid—it is not permissible to slaughter such an animal for sacrifice.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib reported by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and others, authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly forbids animals with these defects.
The Hanafi school relies on this hadith despite it being ahad (zanni al-thubut) because its meaning is clear.
3
Analyze the Hanafi understanding
The word 'لا تجوز' indicates absolute prohibition. The specification of 'obvious' (al-bayyin) means only clear defects invalidate; minor or hidden defects do not. This is the Hanafi principle for interpreting the hadith.
4
Understand the nuance on lameness
The hadith mentions 'al-kasirah' (broken leg that does not heal). Hanafi scholars expand this: if the animal uses its fourth leg lightly, it is permissible; if it completely lifts or drags it, it is not. This shows the school's emphasis on the animal's ability to walk to the slaughter place.
The nuance is from later Hanafi works like al-Hawi.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) have similar lists but may differ on inclusion of certain defects (e.g., emaciation). The Hanafi position is based on this specific hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (لا بالعمياء والعوراء والعجفاء والعرجاء) أي التي لا تمشي إلى المنسك أي إلى المذبح لما روي عن البراء بن عازب أن عليه الصلاة والسلام قال أربع لا تجوز في الأضاحي العوراء البين عورها والمريضة البين مرضها، والعجفاء البين ضلعها والكسيرة التي لا تنقى رواه أبو داود والنسائي وجماعة أخر وصححه الترمذي. وفي الحاوي قال :مشايخنا العرجاء التي تمشي بثلاثة قوائم وتجافي الرابع عن الأرض لا تجوز الأضحية بها، وإن كانت تضع الرابع على الأرض وتستعين به إلا أنها ذلك وتضعه وضعاً خفيفاً يجوز، وإن كانت ترفعه رفعاً أو تحمل المنكسر لا تجوز .
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'Not with the blind, the one-eyed, the emaciated, and the lame' meaning that which does not walk to the place of sacrifice, because it is narrated from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Four are not permissible as sacrifices: the one-eyed whose blindness is obvious, the sick whose illness is obvious, the emaciated whose emaciation is obvious, and the broken [leg] that does not recover.' Reported by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and others, and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. And in al-Hawi: Our shaykhs said: the lame that walks on three legs and keeps the fourth off the ground is not permissible to sacrifice; if it places the fourth on the ground and uses it, but does so lightly, then it is permissible; if it lifts it completely or drags the broken one, it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof. The author (al-Marghinani) states the rule: animals that are blind, one-eyed, emaciated, or lame are not valid for sacrifice. He explains that 'lame' means the animal cannot walk to the slaughter place. He then provides the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib which lists four defects: obvious blindness, obvious illness, obvious emaciation, and a broken leg that does not heal. The Hanafi school adopts this hadith. The commentary from al-Hawi adds nuance: a lame animal that uses its fourth leg lightly is acceptable, but if it completely lifts it or drags a broken leg, it is not. This follows the Hanafi principle of considering the severity of the defect.

Key Terms
العجفاء (al-'ajfa'): The emaciated animal with obvious thinness/scantiness.
الكسيرة (al-kasirah): The animal with a broken leg that does not heal (lameness impeding walking).
المنسك (al-mansak): Place of sacrifice; the slaughter area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following lame animals is still valid for udhiyah?
A) An animal that walks on three legs, completely lifting the fourth.
B) An animal that places all four feet on the ground but limps slightly.
C) An animal that places the fourth leg on the ground but uses it very lightly.
D) An animal that drags a broken leg without putting weight on it.

Key Takeaway
The four defects from the hadith invalidate sacrifice, but the Hanafi school grades lameness based on the animal's ability to use the affected leg.

Defects in Sacrificial Animals: The Hanafi Threshold Dispute
Discussing the ruling on animals with cut ears, tail, eyes, or udder, including intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the threshold.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a cut ear or tail invalidates an animal for sacrifice, and distinguish between the thresholds of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A cut ear or tail invalidates only if more than half is missing—the Sahibayn's view, chosen by Abu al-Layth, is the mufta bihi.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed rules for defects in sacrificial animals, particularly cuts to the ears, tail, eyes, and udder. The hadith of 'Ali prohibits certain types of cuts. The Hanafi school agrees that minor defects are pardoned, but they differ on the threshold for 'minor.' We will explore the views of Abu Hanifa and his two students, and see which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the prohibited defects from the hadith
Study the hadith of 'Ali that lists muqabilah, mudabirah, sharqa', and kharqa'. These are cuts to the front of the tail, back of the ear, long slit, and wide slit respectively.
The hadith is a key source; its command to 'examine' implies avoiding such defects.
2
Learn the general rule: majority takes the rule of the whole
The text states that if most of the ear or tail remains, it is valid because the majority has the ruling of the whole, and minor defects are pardoned. This is the baseline principle.
This principle applies to both remaining and removal; a minor loss is tolerated.
3
Compare Abu Hanifa's threshold (one-third) with the Sahibayn's (more than half)
Abu Hanifa analogizes to bequests: one-third is minor, so loss up to one-third is tolerated. The Sahibayn stick to the literal reality (haqiqah) that as long as more than half remains, the defect is not major.
Another narration from Abu Hanifa gives one-quarter as threshold.
4
Note Abu Hanifa's reported retraction
Abu Yusuf reported that when he informed Abu Hanifa of his view, Abu Hanifa said 'My view is your view,' which some interpret as retraction, others as closeness.
This strengthens the Sahibayn's position.
5
Apply the mufta bihi (more than half remains) to practical cases
The relied-upon position is the Sahibayn's: if more than half of the ear/tail remains, it is valid; if half or less, invalid. This is the choice of Abu al-Layth and later authorities.
For the eye, a special procedure using fodder is described to measure loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ومقطوعة أكثر الإذان أو الذئب أو العين أو الألية) لقول علي رضي الله تعالى عنه : أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نستشرف العين والأذن وأن لا نضحي بمقابلة ولا مدابرة ولا شرقاء ولا خرقاء رواه أبو داود والنسائي وغيرهما وصححه الترمذي. المقابلة قطع من مقدم ذنبها والمدابرة قطع من مؤخر أذنها، والشرقاء أن يكون الخرق في أذنها طويلاً، والخرقاء أن يكون عرضاً وإن بقي أكثر الإذن ،جاز، وكذا أكثر الذنب لأن للأكثر حكم الكل بقاء وذهاباً وهذا لأن العيب اليسير لا يمكن التحرز عنه فجعل عفواً. وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى أن الثلث إذا ذهب وبقي الثلثان يجوز، وإن ذهب أكثر من الثلث لا يجوز لأن الثلث تنفذ فيه الوصية من غير إجازة الورثة فاعتبر قليلاً وفيما زاد لا ينفذ إلا برضاهم فاعتبر كثيراً، ويروى عنه الربع لأنه يحكي حكاية الكل. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: إذا بقي أكثر من النصف أجزأه اعتباراً للحقيقة وهو اختيار أبي الليث. وقال أبو يوسف : أخبرت بقولي أبي حنيفة فقال : قولي هو قولك. قيل هو رجوع إلى قول أبي يوسف، وقيل معناه قولي قريب من قولك. وفي كون النصف مانعاً روايتان عنهما، وتأويل ما روينا إذا كان بعض الآذان مقطوعاً على اختلاف الروايتان لأن مجرد الرد الشق من غير ذهاب شيء الأذن لا يمنع، ثم في معرفة مقدار الذاهب والباقي يتيسر في غير العين وفي العين قال : تسدعينها المعيبة بعد أن جاعت ثم يقرب إليها العلف قليلاً قليلاً فإذا رأته في موضع علم ذلك الموضع ثم تسدعينها الصحيحة ويقرب العلف إليها شيئاً فشيئاً . إذا رأته من مكان علم عليه، ثم ينظر ما بينهما من التفاوت فإن كان نصفاً أو ثلثاً أو غير ذلك فالذاهب هو ذلك القدر.
He said: 'And [not] the one whose more than half of the ears, tail, eye, or udder is cut' due to the saying of 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded us to examine the eye and ear, and not to sacrifice an animal with a cut from the front of the tail, nor from the back of the ear, nor with a long slit in the ear, nor with a wide slit.' Reported by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and others, and authenticated by al-Tirmidhi. Muqabilah is cutting from the front of the tail, Mudabirah is cutting from the back of the ear, Sharqa' is a long slit in the ear, and Kharqa' is a wide slit. And if most of the ear remains, it is permissible, as is most of the tail, because the majority has the ruling of the whole in remaining and removal. And this is because a minor defect cannot be avoided, so it is pardoned. According to Abu Hanifa: if one-third is gone and two-thirds remain, it is permissible; if more than one-third is gone, it is not, because one-third is the threshold for bequest without heirs' permission, so it is considered minor, while beyond that requires permission, so it is major. It is also narrated from him that the threshold is one-quarter, because that resembles the whole. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: if more than half remains, it suffices, considering the reality, and this is the choice of Abu al-Layth. Abu Yusuf said: 'I informed Abu Hanifa of my view, and he said: 'My view is your view.' Some say this is a retraction to Abu Yusuf's view, others say it means 'my view is close to your view.' Regarding whether half is prohibitive, there are two narrations from them. The interpretation of what we narrated is if part of the ear is cut, according to the difference of the two narrations, because mere splitting of the ear without loss of part does not prevent. Then, to know the amount lost and remaining is easy for other than the eye; for the eye, he said: 'You mark the defective eye after it becomes hungry, then bring fodder gradually near it; when it sees it at a place, mark that place, then you mark the healthy eye and bring fodder gradually; when it sees it from a place, mark it; then look at the difference between them; if it is half, one-third, or other, then the lost amount is that.'
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute with proof. It discusses animals with cut ears, tails, eyes, or udders. The hadith of 'Ali lists specific types of cuts. The general rule: if most of the ear or tail remains, it is valid, because the majority takes the rule of the whole, and minor defects are pardoned. Abu Hanifa specifies that if one-third is lost, it is permissible; if more than one-third, it is not, analogizing to the rule of bequests (one-third is minor). Another narration says one-quarter. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: if more than half remains, it is valid, looking at reality. Abu Hanifa's reported interaction with Abu Yusuf suggests either a retraction or closeness. There are also two narrations on whether half exactly is prohibitive. A method for measuring eye defect is described using fodder. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn (more than half remains), as it is the choice of Abu al-Layth and later authorities.

Key Terms
المقابلة (al-muqabilah): An animal with a cut from the front part of the tail.
المدابرة (al-mudabirah): An animal with a cut from the back part of the ear.
الشرقاء (al-sharqa'): An animal with a long vertical slit in the ear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), what is the minimum part of the ear that must remain for the animal to be valid for sacrifice?
A) At least one-third must remain.
B) At least one-quarter must remain.
C) More than half must remain.
D) At least half must remain.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a sacrificial animal is valid if more than half of the ear or tail remains; loss of half or less invalidates.

Species and Age Requirements for Udhiyah
Stating the permissible species and age for udhiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible species and minimum age requirements for a valid udhiyah according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is valid only from thani of camels, cattle, and sheep, or jadha' of sheep.

This lesson identifies which animals are valid for the sacrifice (udhiyah) in the Hanafi school. The ruling is established by divine text and restricted to specific species and ages. You will learn the key terms 'thani' and 'jadha'' and how they apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the permissible species
From the text, note that udhiyah is valid only from camels, cattle (including buffalo), and sheep. Wild cattle are excluded.
The text says 'من الإبل والبقر والغنم'.
2
Understand the age categories: thani and jadha'
A thani is an animal that has shed its first incisor; for sheep, a jadha' (younger, about 6-12 months) is also accepted based on a hadith.
Thani is the standard; jadha' is an exception only for sheep.
3
Apply the hadith evidence
The Prophet said: 'Do not slaughter except a musinnah (thani), unless it is difficult, then slaughter a jadha' from sheep.' This limits the exception to sheep.
Hadith reported by Muslim.
4
Handle hybrid animals
For a hybrid of two species, the mother's species determines the ruling. If the mother is from a valid species, the hybrid is valid.
The text states 'تعتبر الأم'.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school allows jadha' from goats as well. The Hanafi school restricts it to sheep.
This is a point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والأضحية من الإبل والبقر والغنم لأن جواز التضحية بهذه الأشياء عرفت شرعاً بالنص على خلاف القياس فيقتصر على ما ورد وتجوز بالجاموس لأنه نوع من البقر بخلاف بقر الوحش حيث لا تجوز الأضحية به لأن جوازها عرف بالشرع، وفي البقر الأهلي دون الوحشي، والقياس ممتنع وفي المتولد منها تعتبر الأم وكذا في حق المحل تعتبر الأم . هـ. قال رحمه الله : (وجاز للثني من الكل والجذع من الضأن) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: (لا تذبحوا إلا مسنة إلا أن يعسر عليكم فتذبحوا جذعة من الضأن) رواه مسلم.
He said: 'Sacrifice is from camels, cattle, and sheep, because the permissibility of sacrificing these things is known from divine law by text, contrary to analogy, so it is restricted to what is reported. And the buffalo is permissible because it is a type of cattle, unlike wild cattle where sacrifice is not permissible, because its permissibility is known through divine law in domestic cattle, not wild, and analogy is not applicable. In a hybrid, the mother is considered, and likewise in the case of the place, the mother is considered.' He said: 'And a thani from all is permissible, and a jadha' from sheep,' because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not slaughter except a musinnah (older animal), unless it is difficult for you, then slaughter a jadha' from sheep.' Reported by Muslim.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement without proof in the text itself (though a hadith is cited). It is the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The ruling: sacrifice (udhiyah) is valid only from three species: camels, cattle (including buffalo), and sheep (including goats? Actually 'ghanam' includes sheep and goats, but here 'ضأن' is sheep; the text later mentions 'جذع من الضأن' specifically sheep). The reasoning: the permissibility is established by text (nass) contrary to qiyas, so we limit to these. Buffalo is included as a type of cattle. Wild cattle (bison, etc.) are excluded. Hybrid animals: the mother's species determines the ruling. For age: a 'thani' (ثني) is required from all species, meaning an animal that has reached the age of shedding its first teeth. For sheep, a 'jadha'' (جذع) which is younger (around 6-12 months) is also permissible based on the hadith where it is allowed if a thani is difficult to find. The Hanafi school holds that a jadha' of sheep is sufficient, but for goats, a thani is required.

Key Terms
الثني (al-thani): An animal that has shed its first incisor teeth; for camels: 5 years, cattle: 2 years, sheep: 1 year.
الجذع (al-jadha'): A young sheep that is at least 6 months old (or 1 year according to some), before it becomes a thani.
المسنة (al-musinnah): An older animal, synonymous with thani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid sacrifice animal according to the Hanafi school?
A) A 1-year-old sheep (thani)
B) A 6-month-old sheep (jadha')
C) A 2-year-old buffalo (thani)
D) A 1-year-old goat (jadha')

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts sacrifice animals to thani of camels, cattle, and sheep, with a concession for jadha' from sheep alone.

Defects in Udhiyah: The Hanafi Threshold
Explains the hadith on ear/eye defects and the Hanafi-derived rule of majority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith on prohibited defects and apply the Hanafi rule that the majority of an organ remaining validates the sacrifice.

Core Idea
A udhiyah with a missing part is valid if most of the organ remains.

The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded careful examination of the sacrificial animal's eye and ear. This lesson unpacks the hadith and how the Hanafi school derives the threshold for permissible defects, balancing the need for a sound offering with the reality that minor imperfections are unavoidable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its key terms
The hadith from Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Tirmidhi lists four specific defects (muqabilah, mudabirah, sharqa', kharqa'). Define each term as cuts or slits in the ear.
These are the only defects explicitly mentioned, suggesting that other minor defects are overlooked.
2
Understand the general principle
The commentary states that if most of the ear or tail remains, it is permissible. The principle: the majority has the ruling of the whole (al-akthar yujzi'u 'an al-kull).
This is based on the idea that minor defects cannot be completely avoided.
3
Analyze the internal Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa initially set the threshold at one-third (analogizing to wills), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad set it at more than half (majority remains). The latter is the mufta bihi view.
Abu Yusuf reported that Abu Hanifa later concurred with his view.
4
Apply the measurement method for eye loss
For the eye, a practical test using fodder is described: make the animal hungry, then bring fodder and observe where it looks from each eye. The difference in vision indicates the amount lost.
This method shows meticulous attention to evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العين أو الأذن والأضحية من الإبل والبقر والغنم وجاز للثني من الكل والجذع من الضأن عن أبي يوسف رضي الله تعالى عنه: أمرنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن نستشرف العين والأذن وأن لا نضحي بمقابلة ولا مدابرة ولا شرقاء ولا خرقاء رواه أبو داود والنسائي وغيرهما وصححه الترمذي. المقابلة قطع من مقدم أذنها والمدابرة قطع من مؤخر أذنها، والشرقاء أن يكون الخرق في أذنها طويلاً، والخرقاء أن يكون عرضاً وإن بقي أكثر الإذن جاز، وكذا أكثر الذنب لأن للأكثر حكم الكل بقاء وذهاباً وهذا لأن العيب اليسير لا يمكن التحرز عنه فجعل عفواً. وعن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى أن الثلث إذا ذهب وبقي الثلثان يجوز، وإن ذهب أكثر من الثلث لا يجوز لأن الثلث تنفذ فيه الوصية من غير إجازة الورثة فاعتبر قليلاً وفيما زاد لا ينفذ إلا برضاهم فاعتبر كثيراً، ويروى عنه الربع لأنه يحكي حكاية الكل. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: إذا بقي أكثر من النصف أجزأه اعتباراً للحقيقة وهو اختيار أبي الليث. وقال أبو يوسف: أخبرت بقولي أبي حنيفة فقال: قولي هو قولك. قيل هو رجوع إلى قول أبي يوسف، وقيل معناه قولي قريب من قولك. وفي كون النصف مانعاً روايتان عنهما، وتأويل ما روينا إذا كان بعض الآذان مقطوعاً على اختلاف الروايتان لأن مجرد الرد الشق من غير ذهاب شيء الأذن لا يمنع، ثم في معرفة مقدار الذاهب والباقي يتيسر في غير العين وفي العين قال: تسدعينها المعيبة بعد أن جاعت ثم يقرب إليها العلف قليلاً قليلاً فإذا رأته في موضع علم ذلك الموضع ثم تسدعينها الصحيحة ويقرب العلف إليها شيئاً فشيئاً. إذا رأته من مكان علم عليه، ثم ينظر ما بينهما من التفاوت فإن كان نصفاً أو ثلثاً أو غير ذلك فالذاهب هو ذلك القدر. وفي الشرح: ولو أوجب الفقير على نفسه أضحية بغير عينها فاشترى أضحية صحيحة ثم تعيبت عنده فضحى بها لا يسقط عنه الواجب لأنه وجب عليه أضحية كاملة بالنية من غير تعيين كالموسر، ولو كانت معينة وقت الشراء جاز ذبحها لما ذكرنا، ولو أضجعها ليذبحها في يوم النحر فاضطربت فانكسرت رجلها فذبحها أجزأته استحساناً، ولو بقيت في هذه الحالة فانقلبت ثم أخذها من فورها، وكذا بعد فورها عند محمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف. وفي الخانية: عشرة من الرجال اشتروا من رجل عشرة شياه جملة واحدة فضارب العشرة شركة بينهم فأخذ كل واحد منهم شاة وضحى بها عن نفسه جاز، فإذا ظهر منها شاة عوراء وأنكر كل واحد من الشركاء أن تكون العوراء له لا تجوز أضحيتهم ا هـ
The eye or the ear. And the udhiyah is from camels, cows, and sheep. And it is permissible from the thani of all and the jadha' of sheep. From Abu Yusuf, may Allah be pleased with him: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded us to examine the eye and ear and that we should not sacrifice a muqabilah, mudabirah, sharqa', or kharqa' – narrated by Abu Dawud, Nasa'i and others, and authenticated by Tirmidhi. Al-muqabilah is a cut from the front of its ear, al-mudabirah is a cut from the back of its ear, al-sharqa' is a slit in its ear that is long, and al-kharqa' is a slit that is wide. And if most of the ear remains, it is permissible, as well as most of the tail, because the majority has the ruling of the whole in terms of remaining and going. This is because a minor defect cannot be avoided, so it is overlooked. From Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that if one-third is lost and two-thirds remain, it is permissible, but if more than one-third is lost, it is not permissible, because the will is executed by one-third without the heirs' permission, so it is considered little, and beyond that it is not executed except with their consent, so it is considered much. And it is narrated from him that it is one-fourth because it resembles the entire thing. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: If more than half remains, it suffices, considering the reality, and this is the choice of Abu al-Layth. And Abu Yusuf said: I informed Abu Hanifa of my statement, and he said: My statement is your statement. It is said this is a retraction to Abu Yusuf's statement, and it is said its meaning is that my statement is close to your statement. Regarding the half being a preventer, there are two narrations from them. And the interpretation of what we narrated is that if some of the ears are cut, based on the difference of the two narrations, because mere tearing the split without any part of the ear going does not prevent. Then regarding knowing the amount of what is lost and what remains, it is easy for other than the eye. As for the eye, he said: You will slit the defective eye after it becomes hungry, then bring fodder near it little by little. When it sees it in a spot, mark that spot. Then slit the healthy eye and bring fodder near it little by little. When it sees it from a place, mark it. Then see the difference between them. If it is half, one-third, or otherwise, then the lost amount is that amount. And in al-Sharh: If a poor person obligated an udhiyah upon himself without specifying it, then he bought a sound udhiyah, then it became defective with him and he sacrificed with it, the obligation does not fall from him because an udhiyah became obligatory upon him by intention without specification, like the wealthy person. If it was specified at the time of purchase, it is permissible to slaughter it for what we mentioned. And if he lay it down to slaughter it on the day of Nahr, and it struggled and its leg broke, then he slaughtered it, it suffices by istihsan. And if it remained in this state and it rolled over, then he took it immediately, and likewise not immediately according to Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf. And in al-Khaniya: Ten men bought ten sheep from one man in one transaction, and they were partners in them. Each one of them took a sheep and sacrificed for himself; it is permissible. Then if a one-eyed sheep appeared among them, and each of the partners denied that the one-eyed one was his, their udhiyah is not valid.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on physical defects in udhiyah animals and related scenarios. It opens with a hadith from Abu Yusuf quoting the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding the examination of the eye and ear, and prohibiting four specific defects: muqabilah (cut from front of ear), mudabirah (cut from back), sharqa' (long slit), and kharqa' (wide slit). The commentary defines these and then gives the general rule: if most of the ear (or tail) remains, it is valid, because the majority takes the ruling of the whole. Minor defects are unavoidable and thus overlooked. The Hanafi school's internal differences are then presented: Abu Hanifa said that if one-third is lost it is permissible, but more than one-third is not – analogizing to the one-third limit in wills. A narration says he also considered one-fourth. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said that as long as more than half remains, it is valid, which is the preferred view (choice of Abu al-Layth). Abu Yusuf reports that Abu Hanifa later concurred with his view, though the exact meaning of that concurrence is debated. The passage then provides a practical method to measure the amount of eye lost using fodder and marking. Additional rulings follow: a poor person who vows an udhiyah without specifying and then uses a defective animal does not fulfill the vow; if the animal breaks its leg while being positioned for slaughter, slaughtering it still suffices by istihsan; and ten men buying ten sheep collectively where each takes one and sacrifices, then a defective one is discovered and no one claims it – the sacrifice of all is invalid. The key principle is that defects are tolerated only if they are minor (most of the organ remains), and there is a difference of opinion on the exact threshold.

Key Terms
مقابلة (muqabilah): A cut from the front of the ear
مدابرة (mudabirah): A cut from the back of the ear
شرقاء (sharqa'): A long slit in the ear
خرقاء (kharqa'): A wide hole in the ear

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what condition regarding the loss of the ear makes an udhiyah valid?
A) Less than one-third of the ear must be lost
B) More than half of the ear must remain
C) The ear must be completely intact
D) At least one-fourth of the ear must remain

Key Takeaway
A udhiyah is valid if most of the ear or eye remains; the Hanafi school tolerates minor defects because they are unavoidable.

Incidental Rulings: Vow, Accidental Break, and Joint Purchase of Udhiyah
Explains three additional rulings related to udhiyah: vow specification, accidental injury, and joint purchase uncertainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for a poor person's vow, an animal's accidental injury during slaughter, and joint purchase of udhiyah sheep.

Core Idea
Specific circumstances can alter the validity of an udhiyah, such as the intention behind the purchase and the timing of the defect.

Beyond physical defects, the Hanafi fiqh addresses several scenarios that can affect whether an udhiyah fulfills its obligation. This lesson covers three distinct cases: a poor person's vow, an animal breaking its leg during preparation, and a group purchase where a defective animal is later discovered.

Guided Path
1
Understand the poor person's vow
A poor person who vows an udhiyah without specifying the animal must sacrifice a sound one. If it becomes defective, the obligation remains.
The ruling is similar to a wealthy person: the vow creates an obligation for a complete udhiyah.
2
Examine the accidental break
If an animal breaks its leg while being positioned for slaughter, it is still valid by istihsan, provided it is slaughtered promptly.
Istihsan overrides the general rule that a broken leg is a defect.
3
Analyze the joint purchase scenario
Ten men buy ten sheep jointly, each takes one and sacrifices. If a defective sheep appears and none claims it, all sacrifices are invalid because each partner's share is uncertain.
Uncertainty (gharar) in ownership renders the sacrifice invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

مدابرة ولا شرقاء ولا خرقاء رواه أبو داود والنسائي وغيرهما وصححه الترمذي. المقابلة قطع من مقدم أذنها والمدابرة قطع من مؤخر أذنها، والشرقاء أن يكون الخرق في أذنها طويلاً، والخرقاء أن يكون عرضاً وإن بقي Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings on physical defects in udhiyah animals and related scenarios. It opens with a hadith from Abu Yusuf quoting the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanding the examination of the eye and ear, and prohibiting four specific defects: muqabilah (cut from front of ear), mudabirah (cut from back), sharqa' (long slit), and kharqa' (wide slit). Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a source of law that allows exception to analogical reasoning for a stronger reason

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the joint purchase scenario (ten sheep, ten partners), why are all sacrifices invalid if a defective sheep appears and no one claims it?
A) Because the defective sheep was not sacrificed

Key Takeaway

Permissible Species for Udhiyah
States the species valid for udhiyah and the principle of restriction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animal species are valid for udhiyah according to the Hanafi school and explain why wild cow is excluded.

Core Idea
Udhiyah is restricted to camels, cows, and sheep/goats — no analogy extends it.

This lesson covers the species of animals that may be sacrificed for udhiyah. The author explicitly limits the sacrifice to camels, cows, and sheep/goats, based on transmitted texts. We explore the inclusion of buffalo, the exclusion of wild cow, and the rule for hybrids.

Guided Path
1
Identify permitted species
List the three main types: camels, cows, and sheep/goats.
2
Understand the restriction principle
The ruling is based on nass (text), not qiyas; we cannot extend to other animals.
Analogy is prevented (القياس ممتنع).
3
Apply to buffalo and wild cow
Buffalo is included as a type of cow; wild cow is excluded because it is not domesticated.
The author says: 'في البقر الأهلي دون الوحشي'
4
Hybrid consideration
For hybrids, the mother's species determines validity.
In case of mixed offspring, follow the mother.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله: (والأضحية من الإبل والبقر والغنم لأن جواز التضحية بهذه الأشياء عرفت شرعاً بالنص على خلاف القياس فيقتصر على ما ورد وتجوز بالجاموس لأنه نوع من البقر بخلاف بقر الوحش حيث لا تجوز الأضحية به لأن جوازها عرف بالشرع، وفي البقر الأهلي دون الوحشي، والقياس ممتنع وفي المتولد منها تعتبر الأم وكذا في حق المحل تعتبر هـ). قال رحمه الله: (وجاز للثني من الكل والجذع من الضأن) لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا تذبحوا إلا مسنة إلا أن يعسر عليكم فتذبحوا جذعة من الضأن رواه البخاري ومسلم وأحمد وجماعة أخر. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام نعمت الأضحية الجذع من الضأن رواه أحمد. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام يجوز الجذع من الضأن أضحية رواه أحمد وابن ماجه. وقالوا: هذا إذا كان الجذع عظيماً بحيث لو خلط بالثنيات ليشتبه على الناظرين، الضأن ما تمت له ستة أشهر عند الفقهاء، وذكر الزعفراني أنه ابن سبعة أشهر. الضأن والمعز ابن سنة، ومن البقر ابن سنتين ومن الابل ابن خمس سنين، وفي المغرب: الجذع من البهائم قيل الثني إلا أنه من الإبل قبل السنة الخامسة ومن البقر والشاة في السنة الثانية وفي الخيل في الرابعة وعن الزهري الجذع من المعز لسنة. ومن لثمانية أشهر وفي الظهيرية: ولو أن رجلين ضحيا بعشر من الغنم بينهما لم تجز، ولو اشترك سبعة نفر في خمس بقرات جاز وإن اشترك ثمانية نفر في سبع بقرات لم يجز وكذا عشرة وأكثر ا هـ
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: '(And the udhiyah is from camels, cows, and sheep) because the permissibility of sacrificing these animals is known by sacred law through text, contrary to analogy, so it is restricted to what is transmitted. And it is permissible with buffalo because it is a type of cow, unlike the wild cow where udhiyah is not permissible, because its permissibility is known by sacred law, and in domestic cow, not wild, and analogy is prevented. And in what is produced from them (hybrids) the mother is considered, and likewise in the matter of the place, the mother is considered. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And it is permissible for the thani of all and the jadha' of sheep) because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not sacrifice except a musinnah unless it is difficult for you, then sacrifice a jadha' of sheep' – narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, and others. And he said, peace be upon him: 'An excellent udhiyah is the jadha' of sheep' – narrated by Ahmad. And he said, peace be upon him: 'The jadha' of sheep is permissible as an udhiyah' – narrated by Ahmad and Ibn Majah. They said: This is when the jadha' is large such that if mixed with thanis it would be confusing to observers. The sheep is what has completed six months according to the jurists, and al-Za'farani mentioned it is seven months. Sheep and goat are one year old, from cows two years, from camels five years. And in al-Mughrib: The jadha' of animals is said to be the thani except that from camels it is before the fifth year, from cows and sheep in the second year, and in horses in the fourth. And from al-Zuhri: The jadha' of goat is one year, and some say eight months. And in al-Zuhayriyya: If two men sacrifice with ten sheep between them, it is not valid. If seven people share in five cows, it is valid. If eight people share in seven cows, it is not valid, likewise ten or more. End.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This lesson explains the types of animals valid for udhiyah and their minimum ages. The author states the core ruling from the matn: udhiyah is only from camels, cows, and sheep/goats. The commentary explains that this is a restriction based on transmitted texts, not analogy, so we cannot extend to other animals like wild cow. Buffalo, however, is included as a type of cow. For hybrids, the mother's species determines validity. Then the second part covers age: 'thani' (adult) for all species (except sheep where 'jadha' (young) is allowed). The hadith evidence is provided: the Prophet permitted jadha' of sheep when musinnah (older) is unavailable. Additional hadith praise the jadha'. The ideal jadha' is large enough to be confused with adults. Specific age definitions are given: sheep: 6-7 months, goat: 1 year, cow: 2 years, camel: 5 years. The passage ends with a ruling from al-Zuhayriyya on multiple animals and sharing: two men cannot sacrifice ten sheep between them (must each have their own), but seven people can share five cows (each gets a portion) provided the numbers are within the allowed range (1 cow for 7 people maximum).

Key Terms
جاموس (jamoos): Buffalo; included as a type of cow for udhiyah.
بقر وحش (baqar wahsh): Wild cow; not permissible for udhiyah because it is not domestic and has no transmitted text.
متولد (mutawallad): Hybrid offspring; the mother's species determines validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which animal is NOT permissible for udhiyah according to the text?
A) Camel
B) Buffalo
C) Wild cow
D) Sheep

Key Takeaway
Udhiyah is valid only from camels, cows, and sheep/goats; buffalo is included, but wild cow is not.

Age Requirements for Udhiyah Animals
States the age requirements for udhiyah animals and the hadith proof for jadha'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum age for each permissible animal and apply the hadith evidence to allow jadha' for sheep.

Core Idea
The jadha' of sheep is acceptable when thani is unavailable, based on the Prophet's permission.

This lesson details the age requirements for udhiyah animals. The general rule is thani (adult) for all, but sheep can be jadha' if the older is hard to find. The hadith evidence and additional rulings on sharing are covered.

Guided Path
1
Define thani and jadha'
Thani is an adult animal that has lost its first teeth; jadha' is younger, before losing teeth.
For sheep: thani = 1 year, jadha' = 6-7 months.
2
State the general rule
Thani is required for camels, cows, and goats; jadha' is allowed only for sheep.
The matn says: 'وجاز للثني من الكل والجذع من الضأن'.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The Prophet said: 'Do not sacrifice except musinnah unless it is difficult, then sacrifice a jadha' of sheep.'
Narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, and others.
4
Apply the exception
When musinnah (thani) is unavailable, jadha' of sheep suffices.
The exception clause (إلا أن يعسر) shows permissibility.
5
Note additional conditions
The jadha' should be large enough to be confused with thanis; defined ages: sheep 6-7 months, goat 1 year, cow 2 years, camel 5 years.
Al-Za'farani says sheep at 7 months; the relied-upon is 6 months.
6
Sharing rules
Maximum sharing: one cow for 7 people; not more. Two people cannot sacrifice ten sheep between them.
From al-Zuhayriyya: each person must have their own sacrifice if using sheep.

Intention and Share Minimum in Joint Udhiyah
Ruling statement with intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for valid joint udhiyah and apply the rule that each partner must intend qurbah and have at least one-seventh share.

Core Idea
A cow/camel serves up to seven udhiyah partners, each with at least one-seventh share, all intending qurbah.

The Hanafi school permits sharing a large animal for udhiyah as long as every participant aims for closeness to Allah (qurbah). This lesson unpacks the basic rules and an internal debate on two partners sharing a cow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Joint udhiyah (sharing a cow/camel) is permissible under conditions.
A cow/camel can be shared by up to seven people.
2
Note the condition of qurbah
Every partner must intend the act as worship; if one intends only meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all.
This is derived from the principle that udhiyah is qurbah, not mere slaughter.
3
Recognize the share minimum
Each partner must own at least one full share — one-seventh of a cow/camel or one whole sheep/goat.
Shares are calculated as fractions of the animal.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on two sharing a cow
Some Hanafi scholars say two partners cannot share a cow (one would have a half share, which is less than a seventh), but the more correct view (al-asahh) says it is permissible because the half becomes qurbah by being subsidiary to the whole.
The mufta bihi is the permissive view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that two can share a cow/camel; the half share is valid as subsidiary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات أحد السبعة وقال الورثة اذبحوا عنه وعنكم صح وإن كان شريك الستة نصرانياً ومريد اللحم لم تجز عن واحد منهم أو ووجه الفرق أن البقرة تجوز عن سبعة بشرط قصد الكل القربة واختلاف الجهات فيما لا يضر كالقران والمتعة والأضحية لايجاد المقصود وهو القربة وقد وجد هذا الشرط في الوجه الأول لأن الأضحية من الغير عرفت قربة لأنه الله ضحى عن أمته، ولم توجد القربة في الوجه الثاني لأن النصراني ليس من أهلها، ولو اشترك اثنان في بقرة أو بعير لا يجوز في الأضحية لأنه يكون لواحد منهم أسهم ونصف والنصف لا يجوز في الأضحية، والأصح أنه يجوز لأن النصف يصير قربة بطريق التبع لغيره. شاتان بين رجلين ذبحاهما عن نسكهما أجزأهما بخلاف العبدين بين اثنين أعتقاهما عن كفارتيهما لا يجوز لأن في الشاتين أمكن جمع كل واحد منهما في شاة ولا كذلك الرقيق. اشترك ثلاثة في بقرة لواحد ثلاثة أسباعها ومات وترك ابناً وبنتاً صغاراً وترك حصة البقرة فضحى الوصي عنهم بحصة الميت من البقرة لا يجوز عنه لأن نصيب البنت لحم لأنها فقيرة أصابها من ميراث الأب أقل من مائتي درهم، ولو اشترك خمسة في بقرة فأشرك أربعة منهم رجلاً في البقرة تجوز الأضحية عنهم لأن الشركاء أربعة لكل خمسة فتصير الأربعة عشرين وقد جعلوا من أنصبائهم أربعة والأربعة من عشرين أكثر من السبع، ولو كانوا ستة فأشرك خمسة واحداً وأبى الواحد لم تجز أضحيتهم لأن نصيبه أقل من السبع لأن أصل حسابه ستة وثلاثون كل واحد ستة فيكون للخمسة ثلاثون وقد جعلوها ستة لكل واحد خمسة وخمسة من ستة وثلاثين أقل من السبع؛ كذا في المحيط.
And if one of the seven dies and the heirs say: 'Slaughter on his behalf and on you', it is valid. And if the partner of the six is a Christian and desirous of meat, it is not valid for any of them. Or the difference is that the cow is permissible for seven on condition that everyone intends nearness, and difference of objectives does not harm, like qiran and mut'ah and udhiyah, to achieve the objective which is nearness. This condition is found in the first case because udhiyah from another is known to be nearness, for Allah sacrificed on behalf of His ummah. And nearness is not found in the second case because the Christian is not among its people. And if two share in a cow or camel, it is not permissible in udhiyah because one of them would have one and a half shares, and half is not permissible in udhiyah. The more correct view is that it is permissible because half becomes nearness by way of being subsidiary to another. Two sheep between two men, they slaughter them for their ritual, it suffices them, unlike two slaves between two who emancipate them for their expiation, it is not valid, because in the two sheep it is possible to combine each one in a single sheep, but not for the slaves. Three share in a cow, for one three-sevenths, and he dies leaving a young son and daughter, and leaves a share in the cow, and the guardian sacrifices on their behalf with the deceased's share in the cow – it is not valid on his behalf because the daughter's portion is meat, for she is poor, obtaining from the father's inheritance less than two hundred dirhams. And if five share in a cow, and four of them include a man in the cow, the udhiyah is permissible for them because the partners are four for each five, so the four become twenty, and they have made from their shares four, and four of twenty is more than a seventh. And if they were six, and five include one, and the one refuses, their udhiyah is not valid because his share is less than a seventh. The basis of calculation is thirty-six, each one six, so for the five thirty, and they have made six, each one five, and five of thirty-six is less than a seventh. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage addresses various scenarios of joint ownership in udhiyah animals. The key principle is that a cow or camel can be shared by up to seven people, provided all intend the act of worship (qurbah). The first scenario: one of seven partners dies, and the heirs authorize the others to slaughter on his behalf – valid because the deceased had intended qurbah and the heirs continue it. Second: if one partner is a Christian who only wants meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the Christian's intention is not qurbah. The difference is that the presence of all partners' intention for qurbah is essential; a non-Muslim cannot have that intention. Next: two people sharing one cow or camel – initially considered invalid because one would have a fraction (half). But the correct view (al-asahh) is that it is permissible because the half becomes qurbah by being subsidiary to the whole. Then: two sheep between two men – valid because each has a whole sheep (not a share). Contrasted with two slaves for expiation – invalid because each needs to emancipate a whole slave. Next: three partners, one with three-sevenths, dies with minor heirs, the guardian sacrifices on their behalf using the deceased's share – not valid for the daughter because she is poor (inherited less than nisab), so her portion is considered meat, not qurbah. Finally: calculation of shares when adding an extra partner to an existing group, ensuring each partner's share is at least one-seventh (for a cow). Examples: five partners add one, making six – the original five set aside shares from their portions; the added partner's share must be one-seventh of the total animal. The calculation is done to confirm if the share is at least one-seventh; if less, the sacrifice is invalid.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship seeking closeness to Allah.
السهم (sahm): A share in the animal; one-seventh of a cow/camel is the minimum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum share size for each partner in a cow used for udhiyah?
A) One-half
B) One-third
C) One-fifth
D) One-seventh

Key Takeaway
Valid joint udhiyah requires each partner to intend qurbah and own at least one full share (1/7 of cow/camel or whole sheep/goat).

Special Cases in Joint Udhiyah
Ruling statements with applied examples and arithmetic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to rule on joint udhiyah scenarios involving a deceased partner, a non-Muslim partner, guardian sacrifices for minors, and share calculation when adding a partner.

Core Idea
Special cases require careful attention: a deceased partner can be included, a non-Muslim invalidates all, and guardian sacrifices must consider the minor's wealth.

This lesson builds on the basics, covering edge cases from the passage: what happens when a partner dies, when a partner is Christian, when a guardian sacrifices for minor heirs, and how to ensure each partner's share is adequate when a group expands.

Guided Path
1
Scenario: one partner dies
If one of seven partners dies and the heirs authorize the slaughter on his behalf, the udhiyah is valid because the intention of qurbah continues.
The deceased's intention is upheld by the heirs.
2
Scenario: Christian partner
If a partner is a Christian and desires only meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the intention of qurbah is missing for that partner.
A non-Muslim cannot intend Islamic worship.
3
Scenario: guardian sacrifices for minor heirs
If a man with three-sevenths share dies leaving a minor son and daughter, and the guardian sacrifices using the deceased's share, it is not valid for the daughter if she is poor (inheritance less than nisab). Her portion becomes mere meat.
The condition of qurbah requires the beneficiary to be needy? Actually, here the issue is that the minor's wealth status affects whether the sacrifice is valid on her behalf.
4
Scenario: adding a partner to an existing group
When a group already sharing a cow adds a new partner, the original partners must allocate shares from their portions such that each person (including the new member) has at least one-seventh.
The arithmetic example shows how to compute shares.
5
Contrast: two sheep vs two slaves
Two men can slaughter two sheep for their respective udhiyahs because each owns a whole sheep. But if two men jointly free two slaves for expiation, it is invalid because each must free a whole slave individually.
The difference: in udhiyah, co-ownership of a whole animal is permissible; in expiation, the act requires individual ownership.
