وإن مات أحد السبعة وقال الورثة اذبحوا عنه وعنكم صح وإن كان شريك الستة نصرانياً ومريد اللحم لم تجز عن واحد منهم أو ووجه الفرق أن البقرة تجوز عن سبعة بشرط قصد الكل القربة واختلاف الجهات فيما لا يضر كالقران والمتعة والأضحية لايجاد المقصود وهو القربة وقد وجد هذا الشرط في الوجه الأول لأن الأضحية من الغير عرفت قربة لأنه الله ضحى عن أمته، ولم توجد القربة في الوجه الثاني لأن النصراني ليس من أهلها، ولو اشترك اثنان في بقرة أو بعير لا يجوز في الأضحية لأنه يكون لواحد منهم أسهم ونصف والنصف لا يجوز في الأضحية، والأصح أنه يجوز لأن النصف يصير قربة بطريق التبع لغيره. شاتان بين رجلين ذبحاهما عن نسكهما أجزأهما بخلاف العبدين بين اثنين أعتقاهما عن كفارتيهما لا يجوز لأن في الشاتين أمكن جمع كل واحد منهما في شاة ولا كذلك الرقيق. اشترك ثلاثة في بقرة لواحد ثلاثة أسباعها ومات وترك ابناً وبنتاً صغاراً وترك حصة البقرة فضحى الوصي عنهم بحصة الميت من البقرة لا يجوز عنه لأن نصيب البنت لحم لأنها فقيرة أصابها من ميراث الأب أقل من مائتي درهم، ولو اشترك خمسة في بقرة فأشرك أربعة منهم رجلاً في البقرة تجوز الأضحية عنهم لأن الشركاء أربعة لكل خمسة فتصير الأربعة عشرين وقد جعلوا من أنصبائهم أربعة والأربعة من عشرين أكثر من السبع، ولو كانوا ستة فأشرك خمسة واحداً وأبى الواحد لم تجز أضحيتهم لأن نصيبه أقل من السبع لأن أصل حسابه ستة وثلاثون كل واحد ستة فيكون للخمسة ثلاثون وقد جعلوها ستة لكل واحد خمسة وخمسة من ستة وثلاثين أقل من السبع؛ كذا في المحيط.
And if one of the seven dies and the heirs say: 'Slaughter on his behalf and on you', it is valid. And if the partner of the six is a Christian and desirous of meat, it is not valid for any of them. Or the difference is that the cow is permissible for seven on condition that everyone intends nearness, and difference of objectives does not harm, like qiran and mut'ah and udhiyah, to achieve the objective which is nearness. This condition is found in the first case because udhiyah from another is known to be nearness, for Allah sacrificed on behalf of His ummah. And nearness is not found in the second case because the Christian is not among its people. And if two share in a cow or camel, it is not permissible in udhiyah because one of them would have one and a half shares, and half is not permissible in udhiyah. The more correct view is that it is permissible because half becomes nearness by way of being subsidiary to another. Two sheep between two men, they slaughter them for their ritual, it suffices them, unlike two slaves between two who emancipate them for their expiation, it is not valid, because in the two sheep it is possible to combine each one in a single sheep, but not for the slaves. Three share in a cow, for one three-sevenths, and he dies leaving a young son and daughter, and leaves a share in the cow, and the guardian sacrifices on their behalf with the deceased's share in the cow – it is not valid on his behalf because the daughter's portion is meat, for she is poor, obtaining from the father's inheritance less than two hundred dirhams. And if five share in a cow, and four of them include a man in the cow, the udhiyah is permissible for them because the partners are four for each five, so the four become twenty, and they have made from their shares four, and four of twenty is more than a seventh. And if they were six, and five include one, and the one refuses, their udhiyah is not valid because his share is less than a seventh. The basis of calculation is thirty-six, each one six, so for the five thirty, and they have made six, each one five, and five of thirty-six is less than a seventh. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage addresses various scenarios of joint ownership in udhiyah animals. The key principle is that a cow or camel can be shared by up to seven people, provided all intend the act of worship (qurbah). The first scenario: one of seven partners dies, and the heirs authorize the others to slaughter on his behalf – valid because the deceased had intended qurbah and the heirs continue it. Second: if one partner is a Christian who only wants meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all because the Christian's intention is not qurbah. The difference is that the presence of all partners' intention for qurbah is essential; a non-Muslim cannot have that intention. Next: two people sharing one cow or camel – initially considered invalid because one would have a fraction (half). But the correct view (al-asahh) is that it is permissible because the half becomes qurbah by being subsidiary to the whole. Then: two sheep between two men – valid because each has a whole sheep (not a share). Contrasted with two slaves for expiation – invalid because each needs to emancipate a whole slave. Next: three partners, one with three-sevenths, dies with minor heirs, the guardian sacrifices on their behalf using the deceased's share – not valid for the daughter because she is poor (inherited less than nisab), so her portion is considered meat, not qurbah. Finally: calculation of shares when adding an extra partner to an existing group, ensuring each partner's share is at least one-seventh (for a cow). Examples: five partners add one, making six – the original five set aside shares from their portions; the added partner's share must be one-seventh of the total animal. The calculation is done to confirm if the share is at least one-seventh; if less, the sacrifice is invalid.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): An act of worship seeking closeness to Allah.
السهم (sahm): A share in the animal; one-seventh of a cow/camel is the minimum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a joint udhiyah invalid if one partner is a Christian who only wants the meat?
A) Christianity prohibits animal sacrifice
B) The Christian cannot intend qurbah
C) The Christian's share is less than one-seventh
D) The animal becomes impure

Key Takeaway
Edge cases in joint udhiyah require careful attention to intention and share fractions; never include a non-Muslim or a poor minor heir without proper conditions.

Defining Jadha' and Thani for Udhiya Animals
Defining legal ages for udhiya animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of jadha' and thani for sheep, goats, cattle, and camels, and identify the condition that a jadha' from sheep must be large enough to resemble a thani.

Core Idea
A jadha' from sheep is valid for udhiya only if at least six months and appears as large as a thani.

The age of the sacrificial animal is a key condition for the validity of udhiya. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, clarifies exactly what 'young' (jadha') and 'two-year-old' (thani) mean for sheep, goats, cattle, and camels. Understanding these definitions ensures that the sacrifice meets the requirements of the sunnah and avoids confusion with differing opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animal types and their age categories
List the four animal types mentioned: sheep (al-da'n), goats (al-ma'z), cattle (al-baqar), and camels (al-ibil). For each, determine the age for jadha' and thani as stated in the text.
Sheep have both a jadha' (6 months) and a thani (1 year); goats only a thani (1 year) according to the main view.
2
Note the condition for jadha' from sheep
The jadha' from sheep is permissible only if it is large enough that it would be confused with a thani by an observer. This condition is derived from the hadith.
This is a practical requirement—size, not just age, matters.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi variation
Al-Za'farani stated that the jadha' from sheep is seven months, not six. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is six months. Also note the difference for goats: one year versus eight months (al-Zuhri).
The majority Hanafi position is six months for sheep and one year for goats.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school holds that a jadha' from sheep is not valid as udhiya; only a thani (one year) or older is accepted. Their interpretation of the hadith differs.
This cross-madhhab difference affects which animals may be used by followers of each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجذع من الضأن والثني من الضأن والسلام لا تذبحوا إلا مسنة إلا أن يعسر عليكم فتذبحوا جذعة من الضأن»(۱) راوه البخاري ومسلم وأحمد وجماعة أخر. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام نعمت الأضحية الجذع من الضأن» رواه أحمد. وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام يجوز الجذع من الضأن أضحية» رواه أحمد وابن ماجه. وقالوا: هذا إذا كان الجذع عظيماً بحيث لو خلط بالثنيات ليشتبه على الناظرين، الضأن ما تمت له ستة أشهر عند الفقهاء، وذكر الزعفراني أنه ابن سبعة أشهر . الضأن والمعز ابن سنة، ومن البقر ابن سنتين ومن الابل ابن خمس سنين، وفي المغرب: الجذع من البهائم قيل الثني إلا أنه من الإبل قبل السنة الخامسة ومن البقر والشاة في السنة الثانية وفي الخيل في الرابعة وعن الزهري الجذع من المعز لسنة. ومن لثمانية أشهر
And the jadha' from sheep and the thani from sheep. And peace: Do not slaughter except a musinnah (older than one year) unless it is difficult for you, then slaughter a jadha' from sheep. Narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, Ahmad, and others. And he, peace be upon him, said: 'Excellent is the udhiya of the jadha' from sheep.' Narrated by Ahmad. And he, peace be upon him, said: 'The jadha' from sheep is permissible as an udhiya.' Narrated by Ahmad and Ibn Majah. And they said: This is if the jadha' is large such that if mixed with thanis it would be confused by onlookers. Sheep: what has completed six months according to the jurists, and al-Za'farani mentioned it is seven months old. Sheep and goats: one year old. From cattle: two years old. From camels: five years old. And in al-Mughrib: the jadha' of beasts is said to be the thani except that from camels before the fifth year, from cattle and sheep in the second year, and from horses in the fourth year. And from al-Zuhri: the jadha' from goats is one year old. And from eight months.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage defines the age requirements for animals eligible for udhiya (sacrifice) according to the Hanafi school. The text begins by citing hadiths from Bukhari, Muslim, and others that permit the use of a jadha' (young sheep) when a musinnah (older than one year) is not available. It then clarifies that a jadha' is acceptable only if it is large enough to be mistaken for a thani (two-year-old) by the average observer. The Hanafi jurists (as stated in the text) define a jadha' from sheep as one that has completed six months, though al-Za'farani says seven months. For goats and sheep (al-ma'z and al-da'n), a thani is one year old; for cattle, two years; for camels, five years. The author cites al-Mughrib for the general definition: a jadha' is close to a thani but younger. For camels, it is before the fifth year; for cattle and sheep, in the second year; for horses, in the fourth year. Al-Zuhri specifies that a jadha' from goats is one year old, and another opinion says eight months. This lesson establishes the basic categories that determine the validity of an udhiya animal in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الجذع (al-jadha'): A young animal that has not yet reached the thani stage; for sheep, 6 months (or 7); for goats, 1 year (or 8 months); for cattle, in the second year; for camels, before the fifth year.
الثني (al-thani): An animal that has entered the second year of life; for sheep/goats: 1 year; for cattle: 2 years; for camels: 5 years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum age for a jadha' from sheep to be valid as an udhiya?
A) Four months
B) Six months
C) One year
D) Two years

Key Takeaway
A jadha' from sheep must be at least six months old and large enough to resemble a thani; for goats, cattle, and camels, only thani ages apply in the Hanafi school.

Conditions for Valid Udhiya Partnership: The Requirement of Qurbah
Detailing conditions for valid partnership in a cow sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of intention (qurbah) for valid udhiya partnership and identify when a non-Muslim partner invalidates the sacrifice.

Core Idea
For a cow to suffice for seven, every partner must intend worship, otherwise the whole sacrifice is invalid.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq establishes a foundational rule: sharing a cow for udhiya requires unanimous intention of drawing near to Allah. If any partner, such as a Christian, intends only meat, the sacrifice fails for all. This lesson unpacks why intention is indivisible from the act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Udhiya is sunnah muakkadah; a cow suffices for seven partners provided all intend qurbah.
2
Locate the condition
The condition is that every partner must intend worship (qurbah). The text contrasts with Hajj where different intentions (tamattu', qiran) do not harm because worship is common.
3
Analyze the Christian partner scenario
If one partner is a Christian and intends only meat, the entire sacrifice is invalid because he lacks qualification for worship.
4
Examine the dalil
The Prophet sacrificed on behalf of his nation, proving that worship can be performed for others, but only by believers.
5
Derive the ruling
The ruling: any partner not intending qurbah (e.g., Christian seeking meat) nullifies the whole udhiya due to indivisibility of blood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كالقران والمتعة والأضحية لايجاد المقصود وهو القربة وقد وجد هذا الشرط في الوجه الأول لأن الأضحية من الغير عرفت قربة لأنه الله ضحى عن أمته، ولم توجد القربة في الوجه الثاني لأن النصراني ليس من أهلها، ولو أصل حسابه ستة وثلاثون كل واحد ستة فيكون للخمسة ثلاثون وقد جعلوها ستة لكل واحد خمسة وخمسة من ستة وثلاثين أقل من السبع ؛ كذا في المحيط. وكذا الستة نصرانياً ويؤكل من لحم الأضحية ويؤكل ويدخر وندب أن لا ينقص الصدقة من قصد اللحم من المسلم ينافيها وإذا لم يقع البعض قربة خرج الكل من أن يكون قربة لأن الإراقة لا تتجزأ وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا تجوز وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف لأنه تبرع بالإتلاف فلا يتجوز عن غيره كالإعتاق عن الميت. قلنا القربة تقع عن الميت كالتصدق لما روينا بخلاف الإعتاق لأن فيه إلزام الولاء للميت، ولو كان بعض الشركاء صغيراً أو أم ولد بأن ضحى عن الصغير أبوه أو عن أم الولد مولاها ولم يجب عليهما جاز لأن كلها وقعت قربة، ولو ذبحوها بغير إذن الورثة فيما إذا مات أحدهم لا تجزيهم لأن بعضها لم يقع قربة بخلاف ما تقدم لوجود الإذن من الورثة وفي فتاوى أبي الليث : إذا ضحى بشاة من غيره يأمره أو بغير أمره لا يجوز، ولو ضحى ببدنة عن نفسه وعن أولاده فإن كانوا صغاراً أجزأه وأجزأهم، وإن كانوا كباراً فإن فعل ذلك بأمرهم فكذلك وإن كان بغير أمرهم لم يجز على قولهم، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يجوز استحساناً، وفي الكبرى لو ضحى عن الميت بغير أمره لا يجوز وهو المختار وفي رواية تجوز واختلفوا هل الأضحية عن الميت أفضل والتصدق أفضل؟ ذهب بعضهم إلى أن التصدق أفضل، وذهب بعضهم إلى أن الأضحية أفضل. وفي الظهيرية : رجل اشترى أضحية شراء فاسداً فذبحها عن أضحيته جاز والبائع بالخيار إن شاء ضمنه قيمتها حية، وإن شاء استردها ولا شيء على المضحي ويتصدق بقيمتها مذبوحة. وفي الخانية : اشترى سبع بقرة فنوى بعضهم الأضحية عن نفسه في هذه السنة ونوى بقيتهم عن السنة الماضية قالوا : تجوز الأضحية عن هذا الواحد ونية أصحابه عن السنة الماضية باطلة وصاروا متطوعين قيدنا بالسبعة لأنهم لو كانوا ثمانية لم تجز عن كما الواحد منهم تقدم . وفي أضاحي الزعفراني : اشترى ثلاثة بقرة على أن يدفع أحدهم ثلاثة دنانير والآخر أربعة والآخر ديناراً على أن تكون البقرة بينهم على قدر رأس مالهم فضحوا بها لم تجز، ولو كانت البقرة أو البدنة بين اثنين فضحيا بها اختلف المشايخ قال بعضهم يجوز وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث والصدر الشهيد ا هـ.
And if one of the seven dies and the heirs say: 'Sacrifice on his behalf and on your behalf', it is valid. And if one of the six partners is a Christian and intends (only) the meat, it is not valid for any of them. And the distinction is that a cow suffices for seven with the condition that all intend worship, and differences in intention (like for Hajj tamattu' and qiran) do not harm, but for udhiya, the intended worship must be present. This condition is found in the first case because udhiya from another is known to be worship as the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed on behalf of his nation. Worship is not found in the second case because the Christian is not qualified for it. If two partners in a cow or camel sacrifice, it is not valid because one would have one and a half shares, and half a share is not valid for udhiya. The correct view is that it is valid because half becomes worship by way of dependence on another. Two sheep between two men who slaughter them for their sacrifice are valid for them, unlike two slaves between two men who emancipate them for their expiations, which is not valid, because in the two sheep it is possible to combine each one in a single sheep, not so with slaves. Three partners in a cow: one has three-sevenths and dies leaving a young son and daughter, and the executor sacrifices for them with the deceased's share of the cow – it is not valid for him because the daughter's share is meat (since she is poor, inheriting less than 200 dirhams). If five share in a cow and four of them include a man in the cow, the udhiya is valid for them because the partners are four, each having five, so the four become twenty, and they have given four from their shares, and four from twenty is more than the seventh. If they were six and five include one, and the one refuses, their udhiya is not valid because his share is less than the seventh. The calculation is thirty-six, each having six, so the five have thirty, and they make it six, each having five, and five from thirty-six is less than the seventh. Like this in al-Muhit. Similarly, if the sixth is a Christian. And it is eaten from the meat of the udhiya, and it is eaten and stored, and it is recommended that the charity portion not be reduced. The intention of meat from a Muslim contradicts (the intention of worship), and if part does not occur as worship, the whole ceases to be worship because the shedding of blood is indivisible. This is istihsan, and the qiyas is that it is not valid, which is a narration from Abu Yusuf, because it is a voluntary destruction, so it is not valid on behalf of another, like emancipation on behalf of a deceased. We say: worship occurs on behalf of the deceased like charity, based on what we have narrated, unlike emancipation because it imposes wala' on the deceased. If some of the partners are a minor or a child of the master (umm walad), such that the father sacrifices on behalf of the minor or the master on behalf of the umm walad and it is not obligatory on them, it is valid because all of it is worship. If they slaughter it without permission of the heirs in the case of one's death, it is not valid for them because part did not occur as worship, unlike the previous case because of the heirs' permission. And in Fatawa Abi al-Layth: If one sacrifices a sheep on behalf of another, with or without his command, it is not valid. If one sacrifices a camel (badana) on behalf of himself and his children, if they are young, it suffices for him and them; if they are adults, if done with their command, likewise; if without their command, it is not valid according to them. And from Abu Yusuf that it is valid by istihsan. In al-Kubra: If one sacrifices on behalf of a deceased without his command, it is not valid – that is the chosen view; and in one narration it is valid. And they differed: is udhiya on behalf of the deceased better or charity? Some said charity is better, some said udhiya is better. In al-Zahira: A man bought an udhiya with an invalid purchase and slaughtered it for his udhiya – it is valid. The seller has the option: if he wishes, he can claim its value alive; if he wishes, he can reclaim it, and nothing is on the one sacrificing, and he gives in charity its value slaughtered. In al-Khaniyya: Seven bought a cow; some intended udhiya for themselves this year, and the rest intended for the past year. They said: udhiya is valid for this one, and the intention of the others for the past year is void, and they become volunteers. We restricted to seven; if they were eight, it would not be valid for any of them as previously. And in Adahi al-Za'farani: Three bought a cow, one paying three dinars, another four, another one, with the cow among them according to capital. They slaughtered it – it is not valid. If a cow or camel is between two and they sacrifice it, the scholars differed: some said it is valid; and this was adopted by Faqih Abu al-Layth and al-Sadr al-Shahid.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents several detailed rulings regarding partnership in an udhiya animal. The central principle: a cow or camel suffices for up to seven persons, provided all intend worship (qurbah). If any partner intends only the meat without worship, the whole sacrifice is invalid. The text examines various scenarios. First, if one partner dies and the heirs instruct the remaining partners to sacrifice for the deceased and themselves, it is valid because the heirs are competent to authorize worship on behalf of the deceased. However, if one partner is a Christian who intends the meat, none of the partners are valid because the Christian lacks the intention of worship, and the blood is indivisible. The text contrasts this with Hajj tamattu'/qiran where different intentions are permissible. A dispute is mentioned: according to qiyas, a partnership with unequal shares (e.g., one and a half shares) would not be valid, but istihsan (based on the hadith of the Prophet sacrificing on behalf of his nation) allows it because the half share becomes worship by dependence. Similarly, two sheep between two men is valid because each can have one whole sheep, unlike two slaves for expiation. The text then addresses complex cases involving minors, guardians, and permission. It concludes with various ikhtilafat, including the famous disagreement on sacrificing for the deceased without permission, and the choice between udhiya and charity. The relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that sacrificing for a deceased without permission is not valid, but Abu Yusuf's istihsan allows it. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of combining textual proof (dalil naqli) with istihsan to refine rulings.

Key Terms
القربة (al-qurbah): The intention of drawing near to Allah through worship; a necessary condition for the validity of udhiya in partnership.
الاستحسان (istihsan): Equitable preference over qiyas based on a stronger evidence; used in later rulings for partnership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if one partner in a joint udhiya is a Christian who intends only the meat, what is the ruling?
A) Valid for the Muslims
B) Valid for the Christian only
C) Invalid for all partners
D) Valid if the Christian is a guest

Key Takeaway
The validity of a joint udhiya requires that every partner intends worship (qurbah); otherwise, the indivisible blood makes the whole sacrifice invalid.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Unequal Shares in Udhiya and Istihsan
Intra-Hanafi dispute on share validity and istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to resolve the dispute on unequal shares in udhiya and evaluate the opposing qiyas argument.

Core Idea
Though qiyas forbids a half share, istihsan validates it because the blood is indivisible and the majority intention of worship covers the whole.

This passage continues with a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Is it valid for two persons to share a cow with unequal shares for udhiya? The qiyas argument says no because a half share cannot be a valid sacrifice, but the majority Hanafi position adopts istihsan, supported by the hadith of the Prophet and the principle of dependence. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and arithmetic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Two partners share a cow; one has one and a half shares (e.g., one pays for 3/4, other for 1/4). The question is whether the one with half share is valid.
2
State the qiyas position
According to qiyas, it is invalid because each share must be a valid udhiya on its own; a half share is insufficient.
This is also a narration from Abu Yusuf.
3
State the istihsan position
The soundest view (al-ashahh) is that it is valid because the half share becomes worship by being dependent on the whole (bi tariq al-taba'iyya).
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Trace the evidence
The hadith of the Prophet sacrificing for his nation shows representation; the indivisibility of blood means the entire animal is a single worship act.
5
Analyze the share calculation
The passage gives arithmetic examples: in a seven-person cow, each must have at least 1/7 share. If a share is less (e.g., 5/36), the sacrifice is invalid.
This underscores that the minimum share is 1/7.

And if one of the seven dies and the heirs say: 'Sacrifice on his behalf and on your behalf', it is valid. And if one of the six partners is a Christian and intends (only) the meat, it is not valid for any of them. And the distinction is that a cow suffices for seven with the condition that all intend worship, and differences in intention (like for Hajj tamattu' and qiran) do not harm, but for udhiya, the intended worship must be present. This condition is found in the first case because udhiya from another is known to be worship as the Prophet (peace be upon him) sacrificed on behalf of his nation. Worship is not found in the second case because the Christian is not qualified for it. If two partners in a cow or camel sacrifice, it is not valid because one would have one and a half shares, and half a share is not valid for udhiya. The correct view is that it is valid because half becomes worship by way of dependence on another. Two sheep between two men who slaughter them for their sacrifice are valid for them, unlike two slaves between two men who emancipate them for their expiations, which is not valid, because in the two sheep it is possible to combine each one in a single sheep, not so with slaves. Three partners in a cow: one has three-sevenths and dies leaving a young son and daughter, and the executor sacrifices for them with the deceased's share of the cow – it is not valid for him because the daughter's share is meat (since she is poor, inheriting less than 200 dirhams). If five share in a cow and four of them include a man in the cow, the udhiya is valid for them because the partners are four, each having five, so the four become twenty, and they have given four from their shares, and four from twenty is more than the seventh. If they were six and five include one, and the one refuses, their udhiya is not valid because his share is less than the seventh. The calculation is thirty-six, each having six, so the five have thirty, and they make it six, each having five, and five from thirty-six is less than the seventh. Like this in al-Muhit. Similarly, if the sixth is a Christian. And it is eaten from the meat of the udhiya, and it is eaten and stored, and it is recommended that the charity portion not be reduced. The intention of meat from a Muslim contradicts (the intention of worship), and if part does not occur as worship, the whole ceases to be worship because the shedding of blood is indivisible. This is istihsan, and the qiyas is that it is not valid, which is a narration from Abu Yusuf, because it is a voluntary destruction, so it is not valid on behalf of another, like emancipation on behalf of a deceased. We say: worship occurs on behalf of the deceased like charity, based on what we have narrated, unlike emancipation because it imposes wala' on the deceased. If some of the partners are a minor or a child of the master (umm walad), such that the father sacrifices on behalf of the minor or the master on behalf of the umm walad and it is not obligatory on them, it is valid because all of it is worship. If they slaughter it without permission of the heirs in the case of one's death, it is not valid for them because part did not occur as worship, unlike the previous case because of the heirs' permission. And in Fatawa Abi al-Layth: If one sacrifices a sheep on behalf of another, with or without his command, it is not valid. If one sacrifices a camel (badana) on behalf of himself and his children, if they are young, it suffices for him and them; if they are adults, if done with their command, likewise; if without their command, it is not valid according to them. And from Abu Yusuf that it is valid by istihsan. In al-Kubra: If one sacrifices on behalf of a deceased without his command, it is not valid – that is the chosen view; and in one narration it is valid. And they differed: is udhiya on behalf of the deceased better or charity? Some said charity is better, some said udhiya is better. In al-Zahira: A man bought an udhiya with an invalid purchase and slaughtered it for his udhiya – it is valid. The seller has the option: if he wishes, he can claim its value alive; if he wishes, he can reclaim it, and nothing is on the one sacrificing, and he gives in charity its value slaughtered. In al-Khaniyya: Seven bought a cow; some intended udhiya for themselves this year, and the rest intended for the past year. They said: udhiya is valid for this one, and the intention of the others for the past year is void, and they become volunteers. We restricted to seven; if they were eight, it would not be valid for any of them as previously. And in Adahi al-Za'farani: Three bought a cow, one paying three dinars, another four, another one, with the cow among them according to capital. They slaughtered it – it is not valid. If a cow or camel is between two and they sacrifice it, the scholars differed: some said it is valid; and this was adopted by Faqih Abu al-Layth and al-Sadr al-Shahid.

Commentary
This passage presents several detailed rulings regarding partnership in an udhiya animal. The central principle: a cow or camel suffices for up to seven persons, provided all intend worship (qurbah). If any partner intends only the meat without worship, the whole sacrifice is invalid. The text examines various scenarios. First, if one partner dies and the heirs instruct the remaining partners to sacrifice for the deceased and themselves, it is valid because the heirs are competent to authorize worship on behalf of the deceased. However, if one partner is a Christian who intends the meat, none of the partners are valid because the Christian lacks the intention of worship, and the blood is indivisible. The text contrasts this with Hajj tamattu'/qiran where different intentions are permissible. A dispute is mentioned: according to qiyas, a partnership with unequal shares (e.g., one and a half shares) would not be valid, but istihsan (based on the hadith of the Prophet sacrificing on behalf of his nation) allows it because the half share becomes worship by dependence. Similarly, two sheep between two men is valid because each can have one whole sheep, unlike two slaves for expiation. The text then addresses complex cases involving minors, guardians, and permission. It concludes with various ikhtilafat, including the famous disagreement on sacrificing for the deceased without permission, and the choice between udhiya and charity. The relied-upon view (al-mukhtar) is that sacrificing for a deceased without permission is not valid, but Abu Yusuf's istihsan allows it. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of combining textual proof (dalil naqli) with istihsan to refine rulings.

Key Terms
القربة (al-qurbah): The intention of drawing near to Allah through worship; necessary for valid udhiya.
الاستحسان (istihsan): Equitable preference over qiyas based on a stronger evidence; used to validate unequal shares.
التبع (al-taba'iyya): Dependence; a share becomes valid worship by being attached to the whole.
الأصح (al-ashahh): The soundest view; the preferred position among multiple narrations.

A) Valid, because the half share becomes worship by dependence
B) Invalid, because half a share is insufficient
C) Valid only if the majority partner intends worship
D) Invalid, because sharing is not allowed in udhiya

Key Takeaway
Istihsan validates unequal shares in udhiya because the whole sacrifice is a single act of worship; thus even a small share suffices as part of the collective.

Ruling on Eating, Storing, and Giving Charity from Udhiya Meat
Permissibility of eating, storing, and giving charity from udhiya meat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating, storing, and giving charity from udhiya meat, and explain why charity is recommended despite the apparent command in the Quran.

Core Idea
Eating and storing udhiya meat is permissible; charity is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on the meat of the udhiya. While some might assume all meat must be given in charity, the text shows that the owner may eat, store, and share it. The key point is that giving charity is recommended (mandub), not obligatory, even though the Quranic verse uses an imperative. Understanding this distinction ensures that one does not impose undue hardship or miss the reward of charity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The meat of the udhiya. The ruling: it is permissible to eat and store the meat; giving charity is recommended.
The act is not the udhiya itself but the disposition of its meat.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith from Muslim and Ahmad: the Prophet initially forbade eating after three days, then said 'Eat, take provisions, and store.' This permits all three uses.
The hadith is ahad (zanni thubut).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'eat' (klu) is an amr. In Hanafi usul, amr indicates obligation in principle, but here due to the context (lifting a prohibition), it indicates permission (ibahah).
Principle: al-amr ba'da al-hazr yufidu al-ibahah.
4
Handle the Quranic evidence
The verse 'And feed the qani' and the mu'tarr' also uses an imperative. However, the school interprets it as recommendation (nadb) because of the hadith and the consensus that eating and storing are permissible.
The apparent meaning is obligation, but it is overridden by other proofs.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Karkhi) held that charity is obligatory based on the verse. The relied-upon position is that it is recommended, not obligatory.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the mufta bihi is istihbab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤكل من لحم الأضحية ويؤكل ويدخر لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن أكل لحم الضحايا بعد ثلاثة ثم قال : كلوا وتزودوا وادخروا. رواه مسلم وأحمد. والنصوص فيه كثيرة وعليه إجماع الأمة، ولأنه لما جاز أن يأكل منه وهو غني فأولى أن يجوز له إطعام غيره وإن كان غنياً . قال رحمه الله : وندب أن لا ينقص الصدقة لأن الجهات ثلاثة الإطعام والأكل والادخار لما روينا ولقوله تعالى واطعموا القانع والمعتر [الحج : ٣٦] أي السائل والمعترض للسؤال فانقسم عليه أثلاثاً وهذا في الأضحية الواجبة والسنة سواء. ولك أن تقول الأمر لمطلق الوجوب عند أكثر العلماء كما تقرر في علم الأصول. والظاهر من قوله واطعموا وجوب الإطعام والمدعي استحبابه فليتأمل في
And it is eaten from the meat of the udhiya, and it is eaten and stored, based on what was narrated that he (peace be upon him) forbade eating the meat of sacrifices after three days, then said: 'Eat, and take provisions, and store.' Narrated by Muslim and Ahmad. And the texts on this are many, and there is consensus of the ummah on it. And because when it is permissible for him to eat from it while he is rich, then it is more appropriate that it is permissible for him to feed another even if he is rich. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): And it is recommended that the charity portion not be reduced because there are three ways: feeding, eating, and storing, based on what we narrated and on His saying: 'And feed the qani' and the mu'tarr' (al-Hajj 22:36) i.e., the beggar and the one who makes a show of begging. So it is divided into thirds. This applies to both obligatory and sunnah udhiya. And you might say: The command is for absolute obligation according to most scholars as established in usul. And it appears from His saying 'and feed' that feeding is obligatory, and the one who claims it is recommended should reflect.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility and recommendation regarding the meat of the udhiya. The author begins by stating that it is permissible to eat and store the meat, citing a hadith in which the Prophet initially forbade eating after three days but then permitted eating, taking provisions, and storing. This is supported by many texts and ijma'. The reasoning is that if a rich person may eat from his own udhiya, then feeding others, even if they are rich, is also permissible. The author then mentions a recommendation (nadb) that the portion given in charity should not be reduced. He explains that the meat can be divided into three purposes: feeding (charity), eating, and storing. This is based on the verse (al-Hajj 22:36) commanding to feed the qani' (the beggar) and the mu'tarr (the needy who does not ask). The verse appears to command feeding, which implies obligation (wujub), but the author notes that most scholars interpret this as a recommendation (nadb). The author ends by noting that the apparent meaning of the verse suggests obligation, but the school holds it as recommended. This lesson clarifies that the meat of udhiya is not restricted to charity alone; the owner may eat and store it, and it is recommended to give some in charity.

Key Terms
القانع (al-qani'): The beggar who asks for food; one of the recipients of udhiya meat per the verse.
المعتر (al-mu'tarr): The needy person who does not ask but makes his need known; also a recipient per the verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on giving charity from udhiya meat?
A) Obligatory (wajib)
B) Recommended (mandub)
C) Permissible (mubah)
D) Prohibited (haram)

Key Takeaway
The meat of udhiya may be eaten, stored, and given in charity; charity is recommended, not obligatory.

Ruling on the Skin of Udhiyah
Ruling on the skin of the sacrificial animal and prohibition of giving it to the butcher

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on using, selling, and giving away the skin of the udhiyah, and explain why giving it to the butcher is prohibited.

Core Idea
The skin of the udhiyah must be given in charity; selling it is disliked but valid, and giving it to the butcher is prohibited as it resembles a sale.

The udhiyah is a sacred act, and every part of the animal must be handled with care. The skin, in particular, has specific rules: it must be used beneficially, not sold or given as wages. In this passage, the commentator explains the permissibility of using the skin for tools, the ruling on selling it, and the prohibition of paying the butcher from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify permissible uses of the skin
The text states that the skin must be given in charity or made into a useful object like a sieve or bag. This is because it is part of the udhiyah and should be used beneficially.
2
Understand substitution by istihsan
The owner may buy non-consumable items with the skin (e.g., a tool) as an istihsan, because the substitute takes the ruling of the original. However, consumable items like meat cannot be bought with it.
This is an exception by istihsan from the general rule that the skin should not be sold.
3
Analyze the hadith on selling the skin
The hadith 'Whoever sells the skin of his udhiyah, there is no udhiyah for him' is interpreted by the Hanafis as a severe warning (karahah), not invalidation, because the sale is valid due to ownership and delivery capacity.
The phrase 'fala udhiyata lahu' indicates extreme dislike, but the udhiyah remains valid.
4
Examine prohibition of giving skin to butcher
Giving the skin to the butcher as payment for his work is prohibited because it is in the meaning of a sale—it is a compensation for work, thus like selling the skin.
This is makruh tahrimi, a stronger prohibition than selling for money.
5
Distinguish levels of karahah
Selling the skin for money is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked) but the sale is valid. Giving it to the butcher is makruh tahrimi (prohibited) because it is more directly a transaction.
The Hanafi school distinguishes these levels based on the strength of the evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتصدق بجلدها أو يعمل منه نحو غربال أو جراب لأنه جزء منها وكان له التصدق والانتفاع به ألا أن له أن يأكل لحمها ولا بأس بأن يشتري به ما ينتفع بعينه ما لا استحساناً وذلك مثل ما ذكرنا لأن للبدل حكم المبدل ولا يشتري به ينتفع به إلا بعد الاستهلاك نحو اللحم والطعام ولا يبيعه بالدراهم لينفق الدراهم على نفسه وعياله والمعنى فيه أنه لا يتصدق على قصد التمول، واللحم بمنزلة الجد في الصحيح فلا يبيعه بما لا ينتفع به إلا بعد الاستهلاك، ولو باعها بالدراهم ليتصدق بها جاز لأنه قربة كالتصدق بالجلد واللحم، وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام من باع جلد أضحيته فلا أضحية له» يفيد كراهية البيع، وأما البيع فجائز لوجود الملك والقدرة على التسليم. قال رحمه الله : (ولا يعطي أجرة الجزار منها شيئاً) والنهي عنه نهي عن البيع لأنه في معنى البيع لأنه يأخذه بمقابلة عمله فصار معاوضة كالبيع.
He gives its skin in charity or makes from it something like a sieve or a bag because it is part of it, and he may give charity and benefit from it, except that he may eat its meat and there is no harm in buying with it something whose benefit remains, as an istihsan; the example we mentioned is because the substitute has the ruling of the substituted. He may not buy with it something that is benefited from except after consumption, like meat and food, nor sell it for dirhams to spend the dirhams on himself and his family. The meaning is that he does not give charity with the intention of becoming wealthy, and meat is like the hide in the correct view, so he does not sell it for something that is not benefited from except after consumption. And if he sells it for dirhams to give charity with them, it is permissible because it is an act of worship like giving the skin and meat in charity. And the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Whoever sells the skin of his udhiyah, there is no udhiyah for him' indicates the dislike of the sale. As for the sale, it is valid because of ownership and ability to deliver. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'He does not give the butcher's fee from it anything.' And the prohibition of it is a prohibition of sale because it is in the meaning of a sale, as he takes it in exchange for his work, so it becomes a compensation like a sale.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling regarding the skin of the udhiyah. The commentator explains that the skin must be given in charity or used to make a beneficial object, such as a sieve or bag. The owner may also eat the meat and may purchase items with the skin that are not consumable, by way of istihsan (juristic preference). However, he may not buy consumable items like food or meat with the skin, nor sell the skin to spend the proceeds on his family. The underlying principle is that charity should not be for the purpose of enrichment. The hadith 'Whoever sells the skin of his udhiyah, there is no udhiyah for him' is interpreted by the Hanafi school as indicating karahah (dislike), not prohibition, because the sale is valid but disliked. The commentator then emphasizes that the skin cannot be given to the butcher as payment for his work, as this is analogous to a sale and thus prohibited.

Key Terms
الجلد (al-jild): The skin of the sacrificial animal; it must be given in charity or used beneficially.
أجرة الجزار (ujrat al-jazzār): The butcher's fee; it is prohibited to pay the butcher from the skin of the udhiyah.
كراهية (karāhiyah): Dislike; the Hanafi ruling on selling the skin is makruh tanzih, not haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on giving the skin of the udhiyah to the butcher as payment?
A) Permissible
B) Makruh Tahrimi
C) Haram
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The skin of the udhiyah must be used for charity or beneficial purposes; selling it is disliked but valid, and paying the butcher with it is prohibited.

Rulings on Wool, Milk, and Use of the Udhiyah
Rulings on shearing wool, milking, and use of the animal after death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on benefiting from the wool, milk, and skin of the udhiyah before and after slaughter, and to explain the rationale and the intra-madhhab difference.

Core Idea
Before slaughter, every part of the udhiyah is dedicated to the act of worship; after slaughter, the owner may benefit freely.

Sacrificing an animal for Eid al-Adha is a deeply symbolic act of devotion. Naturally, one might wonder: can I use the wool, milk, or even ride the animal before the sacrifice? What if the animal dies before I slaughter it? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies these practical questions, outlining the rulings and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their rulings before slaughter
The text lists several actions: shearing wool, milking, selling milk, riding the animal, and using it for work. For each, the ruling is 'disliked' (makruh). Note the reason: the animal is entirely devoted to the sacrifice.
The phrase 'يكره' indicates a disliked (makruh tanzih) ruling in the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the distinction before vs. after slaughter
After slaughter, the act of worship is fulfilled, so the owner may benefit from the wool, milk, and skin without dislike. The passage explicitly contrasts 'before' and 'after'.
After slaughter, the animal becomes ordinary property.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi difference
Some Hanafi scholars permitted benefiting before slaughter, arguing that the obligation is on the liability (dhimmah), not tied to the specific animal. Understand both positions.
The majority (mufta bihi) holds it is disliked, but the minority view is recognized.
4
Apply the ruling if the animal dies before slaughter
The passage states that if the udhiyah dies, the owner may milk it, shear its wool, flay its skin, and owns all parts without needing to give charity.
This is a separate case: the animal dies before the intention is fulfilled, so no sacrifice obligation remains on that animal.
5
Note the ruling on the skin
The skin of the udhiyah, whether after slaughter or after death, should not be sold to buy vinegar or oil (as per al-Nawadir). This is an additional practical point.
This specific ruling is from Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Nawadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره أن يجز صوفها قبل الذبح فينتفع به لأنه التزم إقامة القربة بجميع أجزائها بخلاف ما بعد الذبح لأن القربة قد أقيمت بها والانتفاع بعدها مطلق له. ويكره بيع لبنها كما في الصوف، ومن أصحابنا من أجاز الانتفاع به يعني بلبنها وصوفها لأن الواجب في حقه في الذمة فلا يتعين ويكره ركوب الدابة واستعمالها، ولو اكتسب يتصدق بمثل ذلك، وذكر محمد في النوادر ولا يشتري بالجلد الخل والزيت فلو ماتت كذا أضحيته فحلب لبنها وجز صوفها وسلخ جلدها فله ذلك ولا يتصدق بشيء؛ المحيط.
It is disliked to shear its wool before slaughter and benefit from it, because he is committed to performing the act of worship with all its parts, contrary to after slaughter because the act of worship has been performed with it and benefiting after it is permitted for him. And it is disliked to sell its milk as with the wool. Some of our companions allowed benefiting from it, meaning its milk and wool, because the obligation upon him is in the liability and is not specified. And it is disliked to ride the animal and use it, and if it earns, he gives charity with the like of it. Muhammad mentioned in al-Nawadir: He should not buy vinegar or oil with the skin. If his udhiyah dies like that, he may milk it, shear its wool, and flay its skin, and that is his, and he does not give charity with anything. From al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage addresses what can be done with the wool and milk of the sacrificial animal before and after slaughter. Before slaughter, it is disliked to shear the wool or milk the animal for personal benefit because the entire animal is devoted to the sacrifice. After the sacrifice, the owner may benefit from these. Some Hanafi scholars even permit benefiting from milk and wool before slaughter as the obligation is on the liability, not the specific animal. Riding the animal or using it for work is also disliked. If the animal earns income, the owner gives charity like that amount. If the animal dies before slaughter, all parts (milk, wool, skin) become the owner's property and no charity is required. The ruling regarding the skin is that one should not buy vinegar or oil with it.

Key Terms
الصوف (al-sūf): Wool of the sacrificial animal; it is disliked to use it before slaughter.
اللبن (al-laban): Milk of the sacrificial animal; same ruling as wool.
موت الأضحية (mawt al-udhiyah): If the sacrificial animal dies before slaughter, all parts become owner's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on using the wool of the udhiyah before slaughter?
A) Permissible
B) Disliked
C) Forbidden
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
Before slaughter, the entire udhiyah is dedicated to the sacrifice, so benefiting from its parts is disliked; after slaughter or if it dies, the owner may take possession without charity.

Recommended Acts and Slaughter by a Kitabi
Recommendations for the owner to slaughter and prohibition of employing a Kitabi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts for udhiyah slaughter and explain why a Kitabi's slaughter is valid but disliked.

Core Idea
It is recommended to slaughter your udhiyah yourself; a Kitabi's slaughter is valid but disliked.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the recommended acts for the owner performing udhiyah and addresses the permissibility of delegating slaughter to a Kitabi (Jew or Christian). It emphasizes personal involvement in acts of worship while recognizing the validity of a Kitabi's dhabh (ritual slaughter).

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act
The author states it is recommended (nadb) for the owner to slaughter with his own hand if he knows how, because performing acts of worship personally is better. Note that delegation is allowed but less preferred.
The Prophet ﷺ personally slaughtered sixty camels out of one hundred.
2
Examine the evidence for witnessing
The hadith to Fatima commands her to witness her sacrifice, indicating that witnessing is recommended and brings forgiveness.
The command 'qūmī fa-ishhadī' (stand and witness) is taken as evidence for recommendedness.
3
Understand the ruling on Kitabi slaughter
A Kitabi's slaughter is disliked (makruh tanzih) because udhiyah is an act of worship and a Kitabi is not from its people (ahl al-qurbah). However, the slaughter itself is valid because a Kitabi is qualified for dhabh (ahl al-dhakāt).
The phrase 'kariha dhabḥ al-kitābī' indicates dislike, not prohibition.
4
Recognize the validity of delegation to a Kitabi
If the owner orders a Kitabi to slaughter, it is permissible (jāza) because the Kitabi is capable of valid dhabh, and the worship (qurbah) is attributed to the owner's authorization.
This contrasts with ordering a non-Kitabi non-Muslim (e.g., Magian) who is not qualified for dhabh, leading to invalid slaughter.
5
Differentiate between types of non-Muslims
The text implies that only a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) is valid for dhabh. Other non-Muslims (e.g., polytheists, Magians) are not qualified, so their slaughter would be invalid.
This is based on the Quranic permission of Kitabi food (Ma'idah 5:5).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وندب أن يذبح بيده إن علم ذلك لأن الأولى في القرب أن يتولاها الإنسان بنفسه وإن أمر به غيره فلا يضر لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ساق مائة بدنة فنحر بيده وستين ثم أعطى الحرية علياً فنحر الباقي، وإن كان لا يحسن ذلك فالأحسن أن يستعين بغيره كيلا يجعلها ميتة ولكن ينبغي أن يشهدها بنفسه لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لفاطمة رضي الله عنها : قومي فاشهدي أضحيتك فإنه يغفر لك بأول قطرة من دمها كل ذنب. وفي فتاوى الفضلي : شاة ندت وتوحشت فرماها صاحبها ونوى الأضحية فأصابها أجزأه عن الأضحية. وفي الذخيرة وكله أن يشتري له كبشاً أقرن أعين للأضحية فاشترى كبشاً ليس بأقرن ولا أعين لم يلزم الآمر ا هـ. قال رحمه الله : وكره ذبح الكتابي لأنه قربة وهو ليس من أهلها، ولو امره فذبح جاز لأنه من أهل الذكاة والقربة أقيمت بإذنه بخلاف ما إذا امر لأنه ليس من أهل الذكاة فكان فساداً لا تقرباً.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: It is recommended (nadb) to slaughter with his own hand if he knows how, because it is better for the act of worship that a person does it himself. If he tells someone else to do it, it does not harm, because the Prophet ﷺ drove one hundred sacrificial camels and slaughtered sixty with his hand, then told Ali to slaughter the rest. If he cannot slaughter well, it is better to seek someone else's help so as not to cause the animal to die, but he should witness it himself, because the Prophet ﷺ said to Fatima: 'Stand and witness your sacrifice, for with the first drop of its blood, every sin is forgiven.' In Fatawa al-Fadli: A sheep ran away and became wild; its owner shot it with the intention of sacrifice and hit it; that suffices for the udhiyah. In al-Dhakhirah: He authorized him to buy a horned, white-eyed ram for the udhiyah, and he bought a ram that was not horned or white-eyed; the order is not binding on him. He said: And it is disliked for a Kitabi (Scripture People) to slaughter, because it is an act of worship and he is not qualified for it. If he orders him and he slaughters, it is permissible because he is qualified for slaughter (dhabh) and the worship is performed by his authorization, unlike if he orders because he is not qualified for slaughter, so it would be corruption, not an act of worship.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage covers recommended and disliked actions regarding slaughter. It is recommended (nadb) for the owner to slaughter with his own hand if capable; performing acts of worship personally is better. The Prophet's example of slaughtering sixty camels himself is cited. If the owner cannot slaughter properly, he should seek help but still witness the sacrifice, as the Prophet told Fatima to witness hers for forgiveness. A fatwa allows if the animal runs wild and is shot with intention. If a person authorizes the purchase of a specific type of ram, and the agent buys a different one, the principal is not bound. Lastly, it is disliked for a Kitabi (Jew or Christian) to slaughter the udhiyah because they are not qualified for worship, but if the owner authorizes a Muslim Kitabi? Actually the text says 'Kitabi' here means a non-Muslim; but then it says if he orders him, it is permissible because the Kitabi is qualified for dhabh (shechita-like), but if he orders a Muslim? There is a textual confusion: the text reads 'ولو امره فذبح جاز لأنه من أهل الذكاة والقربة أقيمت بانابته بخلاف ما إذا امر لأنه ليس من أهل الذكاة فكان فسادا لا تقربا'. This likely contrasts ordering a Kitabi (permissible) versus ordering a non-Kitabi (e.g., a Magian) who is not qualified. The commentator explains: the Kitabi is capable of valid dhabh, so the delegated slaughter is valid, but it is still disliked because it is an act of worship.

Key Terms
الكتابي (al-kitābī): A Jew or Christian; their slaughter is valid but disliked for udhiyah.
الذكاة (al-dhakāt): Ritual slaughter; Kitabi is considered qualified for dhabh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Invalid
B) Permissible but disliked
C) Recommended
D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
Personal involvement in udhiyah is best; a Kitabi's slaughter is valid but disliked.

Mistaken Slaughter: Istihsan Overrides Qiyas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mistaken slaughter of udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mistaken slaughter and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
When both err, the sacrifice is valid by istihsan: the goal matters more than explicit permission.

This lesson examines a case where two people each mistakenly slaughter the other's sacrificial animal. Zufar applies strict qiyas, ruling the sacrifice invalid. Abu Hanifa, however, uses istihsan to uphold the sacrifice, based on implicit permission derived from the designation and urgency of the act. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists prioritize practical objectives over formal analogies.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa) position
The passage begins by stating the ruling: both sacrifices are valid and no compensation is required. This is the position of Abu Hanifa, based on istihsan.
2
Identify Zufar's objection and its qiyas basis
Zufar argues by qiyas: slaughtering without permission is a transgression, like killing a butcher's sheep. Hence the sacrifice is invalid and compensation is due.
His analogy relies on the illa of lack of permission and aggression.
3
Analyze the face of istihsan (implicit permission)
Abu Hanifa responds that the animal was designated for sacrifice, creating an obligation to slaughter it within the limited days. The owner is deemed to have given implicit permission to anyone qualified, as the opportunity would otherwise be lost. This is compared to a butcher tying the legs of a sheep for slaughter.
The designation and urgency generate a strong presumption of permission.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa's view, both sacrifices are valid and no replacement is needed. Under Zufar's view, both are invalid and must be replaced, with compensation for the meat.
The difference affects whether the act of worship is fulfilled.
5
Note the mufta bihi position
Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, endorsed by the later authorities as reflected in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله تعالى: (ولو غلطا وذبح كل أضحية صاحبه صح ولا يضمنان وهذا استحسان والقياس أنه لا تجوز الأضحية ويضمن كل واحد منهما لصاحبه وهو قول زفر رحمه الله تعالى لأنه متعد بالذبح بغير أمره فيضمن كما إذا ذبح شاة اشتراها القصاب والتضحية قربة فلا تتأدى بنية غيره. وجه الاستحسان أنها تعينت للذبح لتعينها بالأضحية حتى وجب عليه أن يضحي بها بعينها في أيام النحر، ويكره أن يبدل بها غيرها فصار المالك مستعيناً بمن يكون أهلاً للذبح فصار مأذوناً له دلالة لأنها تفوت بمضي هذه الأيام ويخاف أن يعجز عن إقامتها العارض يغتريه فصار كما إذا ذبح شاة وشد القصاب رجليها وكيف لا يأذن له وفيه مسارعة إلى الخير وتحقيق ما عينه ولا يبالي بفوات مباشرته وشهوده لحصول ما هو أعظم من ذلك وهو ما بيناه فيصير اذناً دلالة وهو كالصوم، ومن هذا الجنس مسائل استحسانية لأصحابنا ذكرناها في الإحرام عن الغير. ثم إذا جاز ذلك عنهما يأخذ كل واحد منهما أضحيته إن كانت باقية ولا يضمنه لأنه وكيله، فإن كان كل واحد منهما أكل ما ذبحه تحلل كل واحد منهما صاحبه فيجزئه لأنه لو أطعمه الكل في الابتداء يجوز، وإن كان غنياً فكذا له أن يحلل في الانتهاء، وإن تشاحا كان لكل واحد منهما أن يضمن صاحبه قيمة لحمه ثم يتصدق بتلك القيمة لأنه بدل عن اللحم
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if they both err and each slaughters the other's sacrificial animal, it is valid and they do not guarantee [compensation]. This is istihsan. The qiyas is that the sacrifice is not valid and each must guarantee for the other, which is the view of Zufar, because he transgressed by slaughtering without permission and must guarantee, just as if he slaughtered a sheep the butcher had bought. And the sacrifice is an act of worship and cannot be fulfilled by the intention of another. The face of istihsan: the animal is specified for slaughter by its designation as udhiyah, so it became obligatory for him to sacrifice that specific animal during the days of sacrifice, and it is disliked to replace it. Thus, the owner becomes assisted by one who is qualified for slaughter, so he is implicitly authorized because [the opportunity] is lost with the passing of these days, and he fears inability to perform it due to some excuse; so it is as if he slaughtered a sheep and the butcher tied its legs. How could he not grant permission? In it is hastening to good and fulfilling his designation, and he does not mind losing his direct performance and witnessing because something greater is achieved. So it becomes implicit permission, like fasting. From this genre are istihsani issues mentioned by our scholars in al-Ihram by others. Then if it is valid for both, each takes his own sacrifice if it remains, and he does not guarantee because he is his agent. If each of them ate what he slaughtered, each releases the other and it suffices, because if he fed him all initially it would be permissible; even if he is rich, he may release at the end. If they dispute, each may claim the value of his meat from the other, then give that value in charity because it is compensation for the meat.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Zufar. Zufar's qiyas (analogy) argues that if two people mistakenly slaughter each other's sacrificial animals, the sacrifice is invalid and each must compensate because the slaughter was unauthorized, just as if they slaughtered a butcher's sheep. Abu Hanifa, however, applies istihsan (juristic preference): since each animal was already designated for sacrifice, and the time is limited, the owners are deemed to have given implicit permission for the slaughter. The act achieves the goal of sacrifice, so it is valid and no compensation is needed. The text also explains the consequences: if the meat is still there, each takes his own; if eaten, they release each other; if they dispute, they claim the value and give it in charity.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference overriding analogy; used to validate the mistaken slaughter.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogy; the tool used by Zufar to rule invalid.
التضحية (al-tadhiyah): The act of sacrifice; the intended goal behind the designation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa), what is the ruling if two people mistakenly slaughter each other's udhiyah?
A) Both sacrifices are invalid and they must compensate.
B) Both sacrifices are valid and no compensation is required.
C) Only the one who intended correctly is valid.
D) Both are valid but must fast instead.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, istihsan can override qiyas to preserve the validity of worship when error is mutual and the objective is achieved.

Recommendation to Slaughter One's Own Udhiyah
Ruling with proof on personal udhiyah slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on personally slaughtering one's udhiyah, explain the evidence, and apply the conditions for delegation.

Core Idea
Slaughtering your own udhiyah is recommended, not obligatory; delegation is valid but less virtuous.

Many Muslims assume that slaughtering the sacrificial animal must be done by oneself, or that it is obligatory. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position: personal slaughter is a recommended act (mandub), not a duty. The author provides evidence from the Prophet's own practice and a hadith to Fatima, while also addressing the situation of those who lack slaughtering skills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm of personal slaughter
Locate the word 'ندب' in the text. This indicates the act is recommended, not obligatory. Note the Hanafi distinction between fard, wajib, and mandub.
The term 'mandub' is equivalent to sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
2
Follow the first proof: Prophetic practice
The text cites the Prophet slaughtering sixty camels himself. This shows that personal performance is considered the best (الأولى). The continuation 'then he gave Ali the knife' proves delegation is permissible.
The act of delegation by the Prophet himself is strong evidence for permissibility.
3
Analyze the second proof: Hadith to Fatima
The hadith commands witnessing (اشهدي) not slaughtering. This indicates that witnessing is recommended, and forgiveness is promised. The command is specific, implying encouragement, not obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a specific command (amr) to a particular person in a particular context usually indicates recommendation, not necessity.
4
Apply the condition of skill
The text stipulates 'if he knows how' (إن علم ذلك). For a person who does not know proper dhabh, the better course is to delegate, to avoid rendering the animal carrion. But they should still witness.
This condition protects the validity of the sacrifice.
5
Derive the complete ruling
Combine the above: personal slaughter is recommended (mandub) for those who are skilled; delegation is permissible and even preferable for the unskilled; witnessing is recommended for all.
The mufta bihi position is that personal slaughter is recommended, not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيئاً وندب أن يذبح بيده إن علم ذلك لأن الأولى في القرب أن يتولاها الإنسان بنفسه وإن أمر به غيره فلا يضر لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ساق مائة بدنة فنحر بيده وستين ثم أعطى الحرية علياً فنحر الباقي، وإن كان لا يحسن ذلك فالأحسن أن يستعين بغيره كيلا يجعلها ميتة ولكن ينبغي أن يشهدها بنفسه لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لفاطمة رضي الله عنها : قومي فاشهدي أضحيتك فإنه يغفر لك بأول قطرة من دمها كل ذنب.
And it is recommended that he slaughter with his own hand if he knows how, because the best in acts of worship is that one undertakes it himself, and if he instructs another it does not harm, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) drove one hundred camels (as sacrifices) and slaughtered sixty with his own hand, then gave the knife to Ali and he slaughtered the rest. And if he is not skilled in that, then the better course is to seek help from another so as not to make it carrion, but he should witness it himself because of his saying (peace be upon him) to Fatima (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Stand and witness your sacrifice, for every sin of yours is forgiven with the first drop of its blood.'
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
Ruling with proof: This passage states the ruling that slaughtering one's own udhiyah is recommended (mandub), not obligatory. The author provides both evidence and rationale: first, the Prophet's own example of slaughtering sixty out of one hundred camels himself, showing that personal performance is superior. Second, for those unable to slaughter properly, it is better to delegate to avoid making the animal carrion, but they should still witness the slaughter because forgiveness is granted. The hadith to Fatima is a proof that witnessing is recommended. The passage also clarifies that if one instructs another to slaughter, it is valid and the reward is attained, but the personal act is more virtuous.

Key Terms
أضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha as an act of worship.
ندب (nadb): A recommended act, not obligatory. It is meritorious but not required.
ذبح (dhabh): Ritual slaughter by cutting the throat and carotid arteries in the prescribed manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on a person slaughtering his own sacrificial animal?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is recommended (mandub).
C) It is impermissible (haram).
D) It is neutral (mubah).

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering your own udhiyah is recommended (mandub), and delegation is valid, but witnessing the slaughter brings forgiveness.

Edge Cases in Udhiyah: Runaway Animal and Agency
Two fatwas on udhiyah edge cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on a runaway sacrificial animal shot by its owner and on an agent's purchase of a different animal than specified, and determine when intention and authorization boundaries affect validity.

Core Idea
Intention can salvage non-standard slaughter, but exceeding agency authority voids the obligation.

This lesson examines two fatwas from Hanafi sources that address edge cases in udhiyah (sacrificial offering). The first involves an animal that escapes and is shot; the second concerns an agent who buys a different animal than instructed. Both illustrate how intention and authorization boundaries affect the validity of the sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Read the two fatwas: first, a sheep runs wild and is shot by the owner with the intention of udhiyah; second, an agent is authorized to buy a specific ram (horned, white-eyed) but buys a different one.
These are specific cases from Fatawa al-Fadli and al-Dhakhirah.
2
Extract the rulings
First ruling: the shot sheep suffices for the udhiyah (أجزأه). Second ruling: the purchase does not bind the commissioner (لم يلزم الآمر).
Note the different outcomes based on the circumstances.
3
Analyze the underlying principles
First: necessity (the animal is wild) and intention (niyyah) at the time of shooting permit a non-standard method. Second: agency (wakalah) requires the agent to follow instructions; exceeding them makes the transaction void as to the principal.
Intention versus authority: two different bases.
4
Identify conditions and exceptions
For the first, the owner must have intended the udhiyah while shooting. For the second, the principal is not bound unless he later ratifies the purchase.
Intention is a condition for the first; lack of specific authorization voids the second.
5
Apply to hypotheticals
Consider: if the agent buys a ram with a minor defect (e.g., missing one tooth) but the instruction were specific, does it bind? Likely no, unless the principal accepts. If the owner shoots a lamb that went into a neighbor's yard, does intention alone suffice? Yes, if the shooting was necessary.
Edge cases test the boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى الفضلي : شاة ندت وتوحشت فرماها صاحبها ونوى الأضحية فأصابها أجزأه عن الأضحية. وفي الذخيرة وكله أن يشتري له كبشاً أقرن أعين للأضحية فاشترى كبشاً ليس بأقرن ولا أعين لم يلزم الآمر ا هـ.
And in Fatawa al-Fadli: A sheep ran away and became wild, so its owner shot it and intended the udhiyah, and he hit it; it suffices for his udhiyah. And in al-Dhakhirah: He authorized him to buy for him a horned, white-eyed ram for udhiyah, so he bought a ram that is not horned nor white-eyed; it does not bind the commissioner.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
Two rulings: First, if a sacrificial animal runs away and becomes wild, the owner may shoot it with the intention of udhiyah, and if hit, it is valid. This is based on necessity. Second, if someone authorizes another to buy a specific animal (horned and white-eyed) but the agent buys a different one, the principal is not bound because the agent exceeded the instructions. Both are specific fatwas.

Key Terms
الفضلي (al-Fadli): A collection of Hanafi fatwas attributed to a scholar named Fadl or similar.
الذخيرة (al-Dhakhirah): A well-known Hanafi fiqh text by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani or a similar scholar, containing fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the fatwa from al-Fadli, what makes the shot sheep sufficient for udhiyah?
A) The owner caught the sheep before shooting.
B) The owner intended the udhiyah when shooting.
C) The sheep was already purchased for udhiyah.
D) The shooting was witnessed by two Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Necessity and intention can make a non-standard slaughter valid for udhiyah, but an agent must follow precise instructions or risk not binding the principal.

Dislike of a Non-Muslim Slaughtering the Udhiyah
Ruling with proof on the dislike of a non-Muslim slaughtering the udhiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a Kitabi slaughtering the udhiyah and explain the distinction based on the Muslim's instruction.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim can perform dhabh but not qurbah; delegation makes the sacrifice valid.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on whether a Jewish or Christian (Kitabi) may slaughter the udhiyah (sacrificial animal). The text states it is disliked, but if the Muslim instructs him, it is permissible. Understanding the difference between the capacity for ritual slaughter (dhabh) and the capacity for worship (qurbah) is key to grasping this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a Kitabi slaughtering the udhiyah. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked). Determine the level of dislike: in Hanafi, 'karahah' often indicates makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) rather than tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The term 'كره' is used; it does not mean haram.
2
Understand the proof (talil)
The proof is rational: udhiyah is a pure act of worship (qurbah), and a non-Muslim is not qualified (ahl) for acts of worship because they lack the necessary faith and intention.
This is not based on a specific Quranic verse or hadith but on the nature of worship.
3
Apply the distinction: instructed vs. uninstructed
If the Muslim instructs the Kitabi, the slaughter is valid because the Kitabi can perform dhabh, and the Muslim's intention delegates the worship. If the Kitabi slaughters without instruction, the act is not worship and thus invalid for udhiyah.
The text has a minor textual corruption; we interpret 'بخلاف ما إذا أمر' as referring to the case without instruction.
4
Note the practical implication
This ruling means that a Muslim may ask a non-Muslim butcher to slaughter his udhiyah, and it will be valid, though it is slightly disliked. The Muslim should ideally slaughter it himself or have another Muslim do it.
The meat remains halal to eat regardless, but the reward for sacrifice may be affected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وكره ذبح الكتابي) لأنه قربة وهو ليس من أهلها، ولو أمره فذبح جاز لأنه من أهل الذكاة والقربة أقيمت بانابته بخلاف ما إذا أمر لأنه ليس من أهل الذكاة فكان فساداً لا تقرباً.
He (the author) said: And it is disliked (makruh) for a non-Muslim (Kitabi) to slaughter, because it is an act of worship and he is not qualified for it. And if he (the Muslim) instructs him and he slaughters, it is permissible because he is qualified for dhabh (ritual slaughter) and the act of worship is achieved by delegation, contrary to the case where he instructs (?) because he is not qualified for dhabh, so it would be corruption not worship.
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
Ruling with proof: The text addresses the dislike of having a non-Muslim (specifically a Kitabi, i.e., Jew or Christian) slaughter the udhiyah. The reasoning is that the sacrifice is a pure act of worship (qurbah), and a non-Muslim is not considered qualified for such worship in the sense of performing the religious act. However, if a Muslim instructs the Kitabi to slaughter, it becomes permissible because the Kitabi is capable of valid dhabh (ritual cutting), and the worship is fulfilled through delegation. The phrase 'بخلاف ما إذا أمر' likely means if the non-Muslim slaughters without instruction, it would be invalid because he is not from ahl al-dhabh? But the text as given seems to say the opposite: 'ولو أمره فذبح جاز' (if he instructs him, it is permissible) and then 'بخلاف ما إذا أمر' (unlike when he instructs)? There seems to be a corruption; the intended meaning is that if the non-Muslim slaughters without being instructed, it is not valid. The better interpretation: if the owner instructs the non-Muslim, it is valid; if the non-Muslim slaughters on his own initiative, it is invalid. This distinction relies on the non-Muslim's ability to perform dhabh, but the intention for worship is lacking.

Key Terms
الكتابي (al-Kitabi): A Jew or Christian, i.e., a follower of a revealed scripture (Ahl al-Kitab).
ذكاة (dhabh): Ritual slaughter that renders an animal halal; includes cutting the throat and blood flow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a Muslim instructs a Kitabi (non-Muslim) to slaughter his udhiyah?
A) It is invalid because the Kitabi is not qualified for worship.
B) It is permissible and the udhiyah is valid.
C) It is makruh and the udhiyah is invalid.
D) It is haram regardless of instruction.

Key Takeaway
A non-Muslim's slaughter of the udhiyah is valid only if delegated by the Muslim owner, who provides the necessary intention for worship; otherwise, it is invalid as sacrifice.
